2:29:1812:0:14:72:389:700:12:Times:12:Times:Uncertainty and Economic Activity: A Multi-Country Perspective
2:30:1874:14:14:72:414:686:12:Times:12:Times:Ambrogio Cesa-Bianchi, M. Hashem Pesaran, and Alessandro Rebucci
2:31:1938:14:14:72:234:672:12:Times:12:Times:NBER Working Paper No. 24325
2:32:1966:14:14:72:142:658:12:Times:12:Times:February 2018
2:33:1979:14:28:72:203:644:12:Times:12:Times:JEL No. E44,F44,G12,G15
2:34:2002:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:ABSTRACT
2:35:2010:28:14:72:546:588:12:Times:12:Times:Measures  of  economic  uncertainty  are  countercyclical,  but  economic  theory  does  not  provide 
2:36:2112:14:14:72:545:574:12:Times:12:Times:definite guidance on the direction of causation between uncertainty and the business cycle. This 
2:37:2208:14:14:72:545:560:12:Times:12:Times:paper  proposes a  new  multi-country  approach  to  the  analysis  of  the  interaction  between 
2:38:2305:14:14:72:545:546:12:Times:12:Times:uncertainty  and  economic activity,  without  a  priori  restricting  the  direction  of  causality.  We 
2:39:2410:14:14:72:545:532:12:Times:12:Times:develop  a  multi-country  version of  the  Lucas  tree  model  with  time-varying  volatility  and  show 
2:40:2515:14:14:72:545:518:12:Times:12:Times:that in addition to common technology shocks that affect output growth, higher-order moments of 
2:41:2610:14:14:72:545:504:12:Times:12:Times:technology  shocks  are  also  required  to  explain the  cross  country  variations  of  the  realized 
2:42:2713:14:14:71:545:490:12:Times:12:Times:volatility  of  equity returns.  Using  this  theoretical  insight, two  common  factors,  a  ‘real’  and  a 
2:43:2821:14:14:71:542:476:12:Times:12:Times:‘financial’  one,  are  identified  in  the  empirical  analysis  assuming different  patterns  of  cross-
2:44:2926:14:14:71:546:462:12:Times:12:Times:country  correlations  of  country-specific  innovations  to  real  GDP  growth and  realized  stock 
2:45:3026:14:14:71:545:448:12:Times:12:Times:market volatility. We then quantify the absolute and the relative importance of the common factor 
2:46:3123:14:14:71:546:434:12:Times:12:Times:shocks as well as country-specific volatility and GDP growth shocks. The paper highlights three 
2:47:3218:14:14:72:545:420:12:Times:12:g_d0_f1:main  empirical  findings.  First,  it  is  shown  that  most  of  the  unconditional  correlation  between 
2:48:3325:14:14:72:546:406:12:Times:12:Times:volatility  and  growth  can  be  accounted  for  by  the  real  common  factor,  which  is  proportional  to 
2:49:3435:14:14:72:545:392:12:Times:12:Times:world growth  in  our  empirical  model  and  linked  to  the  risk-free  rate.  Second,  the  share  of 
2:50:3539:14:14:72:545:378:12:Times:12:Times:volatility  forecast error  variance  explained  by  the  real  common  factor  and  by  country-specific 
2:51:3644:14:14:71:545:364:12:Times:12:Times:growth  shocks  amounts to  less  than  5  percent.  Third,  shocks  to  the  common  financial  factor 
2:52:3747:14:14:71:546:350:12:Times:12:Times:explain about 10 percent of the growth forecast error variance, but when such shocks occur, their 
2:53:3844:14:14:71:545:336:12:Times:12:Times:negative  impact  on  growth  is  large and  persistent.  In  contrast,  country-specific  volatility  shocks 
2:54:3953:14:28:71:409:322:12:Times:12:Times:account for less than 1-2 percent of the growth forecast error variance.
2:55:4024:28:14:72:189:294:12:Times:12:Times:Ambrogio Cesa-Bianchi
2:56:4045:14:14:72:153:280:12:Times:12:Times:Bank of England
2:57:4060:14:14:72:168:266:12:Times:12:Times:Threadneedle Street

2:59:4085:14:14:72:128:238:12:Times:12:Times:EC2R 8AH
2:60:4093:14:28:72:293:224:12:Times:12:Times:ambrogio.cesa-bianchi@bankofengland.co.uk
2:61:4134:28:14:72:168:196:12:Times:12:Times:M. Hashem Pesaran
2:62:4151:14:14:72:234:182:12:Times:12:Times:University of Southern California
2:63:4184:14:0:72:156:168:12:Times:12:Times:pesaran@usc.edu
2:64:4199:0:14:335:431:294:12:Times:12:Times:Alessandro Rebucci
2:65:4217:14:14:335:520:280:12:Times:12:Times:Johns Hopkins Carey Business School
2:66:4252:14:14:335:448:266:12:Times:12:Times:100 International Drive
2:67:4275:14:14:335:441:252:12:Times:12:Times:Baltimore, MD 21202
2:68:4294:14:14:335:387:238:12:Times:12:Times:and NBER
2:69:4302:14:0:335:422:224:12:Times:12:Times:arebucci@jhu.edu
3:70:4318:0:34:79:192:709:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:1    Introduction
3:71:4335:34:21:79:533:675:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:It is well-established that empirical measures of uncertainty behave countercyclically in the US
3:72:4431:21:20:79:532:654:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and  most  other  countries.1This  negative  correlation  can  be  seen  in  Figure  1  which  shows
3:73:4531:20:20:79:533:634:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the country-specific contemporaneous correlations between stock market realized volatility and
3:74:4625:20:21:79:533:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:real GDP growth for all countries in our panel together with their 95-percent error band.  As
3:75:4718:21:20:79:533:593:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:can  be  seen,  for  most  countries,  there  is  a  strong  negative  association  between  volatility  and
3:76:4826:20:20:79:532:573:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:GDP growth.  On average, this correlation is about−0.3, ranging from a maximum of slightly
3:77:4916:20:21:79:532:553:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:more than−0.5 for Argentina to a minimum of just above zero for Peru.  These correlations
3:78:5005:21:20:79:533:532:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:are statistically significant in the case of most countries, with the exception of Austria, China,
3:79:5103:20:47:79:245:512:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Indonesia, Peru, and South Africa.
3:80:5137:47:99:102:509:465:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f9:Figure 1Country-specific Correlations Between Volatility and Growth
3:81:5448:99:0:129:143:366:6:g_d0_f10:6:g_d0_f10:-0.5
3:82:5452:0:0:138:142:402:6:g_d0_f10:6:g_d0_f10:0
3:83:5453:0:163:132:143:439:6:g_d0_f10:6:g_d0_f10:0.5
3:84:5467:163:11:84:527:276:9:g_d0_f9:9:g_d0_f11:Note. Correlations between (log) realized stock market volatility and real GDP growth. The dots represent the
3:85:5576:11:11:84:526:265:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:country-specific contemporaneous correlations, and the lines represent 95% confidence intervals.  See equation
3:86:5686:11:11:84:526:254:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:(64) in Section 5 for a definition of realized volatility at quarterly frequency and Section 6 for a description of
3:87:5801:11:32:84:260:243:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:the data.  Sample period:  1993:Q1-2011:Q2.
3:88:5844:32:20:96:533:211:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Interpreting  correlations  in  economic  terms  is  difficult  because  causation  can  run  in  both
3:89:5946:20:20:79:533:191:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:directions.  From a theoretical standpoint, uncertainty can cause economic activity to slowdown
3:90:6041:20:21:79:533:171:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and even contract through a variety of mechanisms, both on the household side via precaution-
3:91:6134:21:16:79:533:150:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:ary savings (Kimball, 1990) and on the firm side via investment delays or other forms of frictions
3:92:6232:16:15:91:532:134:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:1For the evidence on the US see,  for example,  Schwert (1989a) and Schwert (1989b) using the volatility of
3:93:6339:15:11:79:533:119:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:aggregate stock market returns; Campbell et al. (2001), Bloom et al. (2007), and Gilchrist et al. (2013) using the
3:94:6453:11:11:79:533:108:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:volatility of firm-level stock returns;  Bloom et al. (2012) and Bachmann and Bayer (2013) using the volatility
3:95:6564:11:11:79:533:97:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:of plant, firm, industry and aggregate output and productivity; Popescu and Smets (2010) and Bachmann et al.
3:96:6672:11:11:79:533:86:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:(2013) using the behavior of expectations’ disagreement.  For the evidence on other countries see, for instance,
3:97:6784:11:0:79:458:75:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:Baker and Bloom (2013), Carriere-Swallow and Cespedes (2013), and Nakamura et al. (2017).
4:98:6874:0:21:79:533:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(see for instance Bernanke (1983), Dixit and Pindyck (1994) and, more recently, Bloom (2009)),
4:99:6968:21:20:79:532:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:or financial frictions (Christiano et al., 2014, Gilchrist et al., 2013, Arellano et al., 2012).2But
4:100:7068:20:20:79:533:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:it is also possible that uncertainty responds to fluctuations in economic activity.  For instance,
4:101:7166:20:21:79:533:648:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Bansal et al. (2005) show that fluctuations in expected growth directly affect asset valuations,
4:102:7262:21:20:79:533:627:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and information regarding future expected growth is encoded in current asset valuations.  In-
4:103:7355:20:20:79:533:607:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:deed, the theoretical literature highlights mechanisms through which spikes in uncertainty may
4:104:7449:20:21:79:533:587:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:be  the  result  of  adverse  economic  conditions.   Examples  based  on  information  and  financial
4:105:7551:21:20:79:533:566:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:frictions include Van Nieuwerburgh and Veldkamp (2006), Fostel and Geanakoplos (2012), and
4:106:7641:20:20:79:532:546:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Ilut  et  al.  (2017).3Theory,  therefore,  does  not  provide  a  definite  guidance  as  how  to  inter-
4:107:7747:20:21:79:533:526:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:pret the countercyclical nature of empirical measures of uncertainty.  In this paper, we employ a
4:108:7844:21:20:79:533:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:multi-country approach to the analysis of interaction between uncertainty and economic activity,
4:109:7940:20:23:79:383:485:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:without restricting the direction of economic causation apriori.
4:110:8004:23:21:96:533:462:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We first develop a simple multi-country version of the Lucas (1978) tree model with time-
4:111:8093:21:20:79:533:441:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:varying volatility in which output or dividend growth rates are determined by a global technology
4:112:8190:20:20:79:533:421:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(or global growth) factor.  We show that country-specific equity returns are driven by two shocks,
4:113:8288:20:20:79:533:401:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the first being the innovation to the global technology factor and the second being the innovation
4:114:8386:20:21:79:533:381:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to  its  volatility.   In  effect,  we  develop  a  consumption-based  international  asset  pricing  model
4:115:8493:21:20:79:533:360:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:where at least two factors are needed to explain the cross country differences of equity returns,
4:116:8590:20:23:79:529:340:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:even though only one factor is sufficient to explain cross country differences in output growth.
4:117:8686:23:21:96:533:317:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:This theoretical insight forms the basis of our econometric identification strategy.  We mea-
4:118:8779:21:20:79:533:296:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:sure uncertainty and activity with realized equity market volatility and real GDP growth, and
4:119:8872:20:20:79:533:276:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:assume that volatility and growth can be driven by two common factors,  as well as country-
4:120:8963:20:21:79:533:256:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:specific volatility and growth shocks.  We identify the two common factors by assuming that
4:121:9054:21:20:79:533:235:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:innovations  to  volatility  and  growth  have  different  patterns  of  correlations  across  countries.
4:122:9159:20:20:79:533:215:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Specifically, we suppose that one of the factors, which we label as “real”, is sufficient to model
4:123:9257:20:21:79:532:195:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:cross-countrycorrelationsof  output  growth  innovations,  but  a  second  factor,  which  we  label
4:124:9357:21:15:79:533:174:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:as “financial”, is also needed to model the cross-countrycorrelationsof volatility innovations.
4:125:9452:15:15:91:532:159:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:2Pricing frictions and the zero lower bound on nominal interest rates can also amplify the impact of a volatility
4:126:9565:15:7:79:461:144:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:shock (Fernandez-Villaverde et al. (2011), Basu and Bundick (2017), Born and Pfeifer (2014)).
4:127:9658:7:15:91:532:137:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:3Theoretically, the impact of uncertainty on activity could even be positive.  For example Mirman (1971) shows
4:128:9768:15:11:79:533:122:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:that, if there is a precautionary motive for savings, then higher volatility would lead to higher investments.  Oi
4:129:9882:11:11:79:533:111:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:(1961), Hartman (1976) and Abel (1983) show that if labor can be freely adjusted, the marginal revenue product
4:130:9992:11:11:79:533:100:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:of capital is convex in price; in this case, uncertainty may increase the level of the capital stock and, therefore,
4:131:10108:11:0:79:529:89:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:investment.  However, these theories are not consistent with the countercyclical nature of uncertainty measures.
5:132:10221:0:21:79:532:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Specifically, we assumeweakcross-country dependence of growth innovations andstrongcross-
5:133:10310:21:20:79:533:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:country  dependence  of  volatility  innovations  (in  the  sense  of  Chudik  et  al.,  2011).   This  is
5:134:10416:20:20:79:533:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:equivalent to assuming that volatility innovations share at least one more strong common factor
5:135:10511:20:21:79:533:648:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:than growth innovations.  As the paper shows, under this condition, the real common factor is
5:136:10604:21:20:79:533:627:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:proportional to world GDP growth, measured as the weighted average of country-specific growth
5:137:10697:20:20:79:533:607:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:rates.4Also, if it is further assumed that the volatility series shareonly  oneadditional strong
5:138:10793:20:21:79:533:587:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:factor as compared to the growth innovations, the loading matrix on the global factors becomes
5:139:10887:21:20:79:533:566:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:triangular,  with  country-specific  volatilities  loading  contemporaneously  on  both  the  real  and
5:140:10990:20:20:79:533:546:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:financial factor, and country growth rates loading only on the real factor.  Under this condition,
5:141:11088:20:21:79:533:526:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the  second  factor,  common  only  to  the  volatility  series,  can  then  be  identified  in  our  model
5:142:11195:21:20:79:533:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and measured in the data as the residual of a OLS regression of world volatility on world GDP
5:143:11288:20:23:79:115:485:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:growth.
5:144:11295:23:21:96:533:462:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Our identification assumptions are in accordance with patterns of cross-country correlation
5:145:11386:21:20:79:533:441:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:that  we  document  in  the  data,  as  well  as  statistical  tests  of  the  cross-country  dependence  of
5:146:11494:20:20:79:533:421:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the estimated country-specific volatility and growth innovations.  For instance, for each country
5:147:11591:20:20:79:533:401:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:in our sample, Figure 2 plots the average pair-wise correlation of volatility and output growth
5:148:11686:20:21:79:533:381:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:series, together with the average across all countries.5It can be seen that the average pair-wise
5:149:11783:21:20:79:533:360:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:correlation across all countries for the volatility series is more than twice the average for the
5:150:11880:20:20:79:532:340:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:growth series, at 0.58 and 0.27, respectively (the two dotted lines).  This evidence suggests that,
5:151:11979:20:21:79:532:320:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:indeed, the volatility series are much more correlated across countries than the growth series.6
5:152:12075:21:20:79:533:299:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We also find even more striking differences when we consider the cross-country dependence of
5:153:12167:20:23:79:342:279:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the volatility and growth innovations (See Section 7.2).
5:154:12223:23:21:96:533:256:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:To measure economic uncertainty, we build on the contributions of Andersen et al. (2001,
5:155:12311:21:20:79:533:235:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:2003)  and  Barndorff-Nielsen  and  Shephard  (2002,  2004)  and  compute  realized  equity  price
5:156:12409:20:20:79:533:215:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:volatility for a given quarter by using daily returns for 32 advanced and emerging economies
5:157:12501:20:21:79:533:195:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:representing more than 90 percent of the world economy.  We also consider several other proxies
5:158:12596:21:15:79:533:174:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:for uncertainty and argue that they are either not suitable for the purpose of our analysis, or
5:159:12691:15:15:91:532:159:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:4Our  identification  assumption  is  compatible  with  the  view  that  the  global  financial  cycle  (e.g.  Rey,  2013)
5:160:12813:15:11:79:533:144:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:is stronger than the international business cycle (e.g., Kose et al. (2003)), with realized equity market volatility
5:161:12929:11:7:79:356:133:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:co-moving more closely across countries than real GDP growth does.
5:162:12995:7:15:91:532:126:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:5The average pair-wise correlation of a variablexfor countryi(i.e., each bar in Figure 2) is defined as the
5:163:13102:15:7:79:532:111:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:average bilateral correlation ofxitwithxjtfor allj6=i.  See equation (65) in Section 6 for a more formal definition.
5:164:13218:7:15:91:532:104:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:6We  note  here  that  these  patterns  of  cross-country  correlations  are  consistent  with  those  documented  by
5:165:13335:15:11:79:533:89:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:Tesar (1995), Colacito and Croce (2011), and Lewis and Liu (2015) for consumption growth and equity returns,
5:166:13443:11:0:79:128:78:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:respectively.
6:167:13457:0:119:116:495:698:11:g_d0_f8:11:g_d0_f9:Figure 2Average Pair-wise Correlations of Volatility and Growth
6:168:13764:119:0:129:143:579:6:g_d0_f17:6:g_d0_f17:-0.2
6:169:13768:0:0:138:142:599:6:g_d0_f17:6:g_d0_f17:0
6:170:13769:0:0:132:143:619:6:g_d0_f17:6:g_d0_f17:0.2
6:171:13772:0:0:132:143:639:6:g_d0_f17:6:g_d0_f17:0.4
6:172:13775:0:148:132:143:659:6:g_d0_f17:6:g_d0_f17:0.6
6:173:13789:148:11:84:527:511:9:g_d0_f9:9:g_d0_f11:Note.  For each country, the light (yellow) and the dark (blue) bar represent the average pair-wise correlation
6:174:13900:11:10:84:526:500:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:with  the  remaining  countries  in  the  sample  for  volatility  and  GDP  growth  series,  respectively.   The  dotted
6:175:14021:10:11:84:526:490:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:lines  correspond  to  the  overall  average  across  all  countries,  equal  to  0.55  and  0.27  for  volatility  and  GDP
6:176:14145:11:11:84:526:479:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:growth,  respectively.   The  average  pair-wise  correlation  of  a  variablexitin  countryiis  the  average  of  the
6:177:14263:11:11:84:526:468:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:contemporaneous correlation betweenxitandxjtfor allj6=i.  See equation (64) in Section 5 for a definition of
6:178:14371:11:33:84:522:457:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:the realized volatility measure and Section 6 for a description of the data.  Sample period:  1993:Q1-2011:Q2.
6:179:14481:33:20:79:533:424:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:not readily available for a large number of countries over a sufficiently long period needed for
6:180:14577:20:23:79:419:404:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:our analysis, or that they are closely associated with realized volatility.
6:181:14652:23:21:96:533:381:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The empirical analysis yields a rich set of findings.  Here we highlight three main results.
6:182:14744:21:20:79:533:360:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:First, and most importantly, we find that the bulk of the negative correlations between volatility
6:183:14842:20:20:79:533:340:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and  output  growth  observed  in  the  data  can  be  accounted  for  by  the  real  common  factor.
6:184:14943:20:21:79:533:320:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:While  unconditionally  volatility  behaves  countercyclically  for  all  but  one  of  the  32  countries
6:185:15049:21:20:79:533:299:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:in  our  sample,  when  we  condition  on  the  real  factor,  the  correlations  between  volatility  and
6:186:15155:20:20:79:533:279:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:growth  innovations  become  statistically  insignificant  in  all  but  two  emerging  economies,  and
6:187:15258:20:21:79:533:259:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:quantitatively much smaller in all countries (changing sign in more than half of the cases).  This
6:188:15356:21:20:79:533:238:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:result does not depend on any auxiliary assumptions made, including that volatility series share
6:189:15452:20:20:79:533:218:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:only one additional strong factor, and suggests that part of the explanatory power attributed
6:190:15545:20:21:79:533:198:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to uncertainty shocks in empirical studies of individual countries, considered in isolation from
6:191:15641:21:20:79:533:177:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the rest of the world economy, might be due to omitting such a real common factor from the
6:192:15731:20:23:79:119:157:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:analysis.
6:193:15740:23:21:96:533:134:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Second,  the  paper  shows  that  the  time-variation  of  country-specific  volatility  is  explained
6:194:15842:21:20:79:533:113:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:largely by shocks to the financial factor (with a share of forecast error variance larger than 60%)
6:195:15941:20:20:79:533:93:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and innovations to country-specific volatility series themselves (with a share of forecast error
6:196:16037:20:0:79:533:73:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:variance of about 35 percent).  Shocks to the real common factor and to country-specific growth
7:197:16133:0:21:79:533:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:innovations explain less than 5 percent of volatility forecast error variance.  We interpret this
7:198:16230:21:20:79:533:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:evidence as suggesting that the endogenous component of country-specific volatility is small, or,
7:199:16327:20:23:79:521:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:equivalently, that volatility measured at quarterly frequency is largely an exogenous process.
7:200:16421:23:21:96:533:645:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Third  and  finally,  we  find  that  shocks  to  the  common  financial  factor  explain  about  10%
7:201:16522:21:20:79:533:624:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of the forecast error variance of output growth,  even though they have strong and persistent
7:202:16615:20:20:79:532:604:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:contractionary  effects.   In  contrast,  country-specific  volatility  shocks  explain  only  1−2  per-
7:203:16719:20:21:79:533:584:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:cent of country-specific forecast error growth variance.  These results illustrate the quantitative
7:204:16818:21:20:79:533:563:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:importance  of  distinguishing  between  common  and  country-specific  volatility  shocks.   In  our
7:205:16919:20:20:79:533:543:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:empirical model, the forecast error variance of output growth is explained mainly by innovations
7:206:17015:20:21:79:533:523:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to country-specific growth rates themselves (with a share of at least 60% percent) and the real
7:207:17110:21:23:79:346:502:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:common factor (with another 25% percent of the total).
7:208:17164:23:20:96:532:479:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:The paper is closely related to three strands of empirical literature on volatility and growth.7
7:209:17260:20:20:79:533:459:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The first strand acknowledges that uncertainty may be endogenous and could be driven by the
7:210:17351:20:21:79:533:439:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:business cycle (See, for instance, Ludvigson et al. (2015), Clark et al. (2016), and Berger et al.
7:211:17449:21:20:79:532:418:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(2017)).8A key difference relative to these contributions, is that our identification assumptions
7:212:17546:20:20:79:533:398:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:apply to a cross-section of countries, as opposed to a single country considered in isolation from
7:213:17644:20:21:79:533:378:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the rest of the world,  or the global economy analyzed as a single,  closed economy.  Also,  our
7:214:17740:21:20:79:533:357:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:identification strategy is simpler and consistent with observable cross-country correlation prop-
7:215:17837:20:20:79:533:337:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:erties  of  the  data  and  the  estimated  country-specific  innovations  as  opposed  to  unobservable
7:216:17941:20:21:79:533:317:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:theoretical conditions.  Interestingly, despite the different approaches taken to proxy for uncer-
7:217:18039:21:20:79:533:296:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:tainty and to separate endogenous responses to the business cycle from exogenous changes, we
7:218:18131:20:20:79:533:276:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:reach similar conclusions that the endogenous component of country-specific volatility is small,
7:219:18227:20:21:79:533:256:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and exogenous shifts in uncertainty can be quite harmful for output growth.  According to our
7:220:18320:21:20:79:533:235:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:analysis, however, the latter applies only to the global component of uncertainty that cannot
7:221:18413:20:20:79:533:215:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:be identified separately in the empirical frameworks that focus on individual countries, taken in
7:222:18510:20:23:79:293:195:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:isolation from the rest of the world economy.
7:223:18555:23:21:96:533:172:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A second strand of the literature has an international focus as in our paper.  For instance,
7:224:18647:21:20:79:533:151:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Carriere-Swallow and Cespedes (2013) estimate a battery of 40 small open economy VARs for
7:225:18736:20:16:79:533:131:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:advanced and emerging economies in which the US VIX index is assumed to be exogenous and
7:226:18824:16:15:91:532:115:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:7The literature is voluminous.  See Bloom (2014) for a recent survey.  Here we focus only on studies directly
7:227:18933:15:7:79:163:100:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:related to our paper.
7:228:18954:7:15:91:532:93:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:8Diebold and Yilmaz (2010) is an early attempt to separate macroeconomic and financial uncertainty without
7:229:19060:15:0:79:200:78:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:addressing endogeneity issues.
8:230:19091:0:21:79:533:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:identification  is  achieved  imposing  country-by-country  restrictions.   Baker  and  Bloom  (2013)
8:231:19192:21:20:79:533:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:study  an  unbalanced  panel  of  60  countries,  documenting  the  counter-cyclicality  of  different
8:232:19294:20:20:79:533:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:proxies for uncertainty, such as stock market volatility, sovereign bond yields volatility, exchange
8:233:19394:20:21:79:533:648:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:rate volatility and GDP forecast disagreement, and use measures of disaster risk as instruments.
8:234:19490:21:20:79:533:627:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Hirata et al. (2012) estimate a factor-augmented VAR (FAVAR), with factors computed based
8:235:19579:20:20:79:533:607:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:on  data  for  18  advanced  economies,  and  use  a  recursive  identification  scheme  in  which  the
8:236:19682:20:21:79:533:587:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:volatility variable is ordered first in the VAR. Carriero et al. (2017) estimate a large Bayesian
8:237:19779:21:20:79:533:566:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:VAR  with  exogenously  driven  stochastic  volatility  to  quantify  the  impact  of  macroeconomic
8:238:19879:20:20:79:533:546:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:uncertainty on OECD economies.  Hirata et al. (2012), Carriere-Swallow and Cespedes (2013),
8:239:19970:20:21:79:533:526:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Carriero et al. (2017) therefore, restrict the direction of economic causation from the outset of the
8:240:20071:21:20:79:533:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:analysis assuming that the uncertainty proxy used is exogenous.  In addition, in our framework,
8:241:20166:20:20:79:533:485:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:countries interact with each other not only via the common factors, but also via an unrestricted
8:242:20262:20:21:79:533:465:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:variance-covariance matrix of the country-specific volatility and growth innovations.  In contrast,
8:243:20361:21:20:79:533:444:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:in the above studies, economies can interact only via common factors or variables like the VIX
8:244:20455:20:23:79:417:424:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:index, but do not interact with each other via other spillover channels.
8:245:20527:23:20:96:533:401:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Our  paper  also  relates  to  contributions  in  the  finance  literature.   The  closest  analogous
8:246:20628:20:21:79:533:381:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to  the  framework  we  propose  are  mean-variance  frontier  models—discussed,  for  example,  by
8:247:20727:21:20:79:533:360:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Black (1976) and French et al. (1987).  In those models, however, the focus is on possible causal
8:248:20824:20:20:79:533:340:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:relations between the stock market return and its volatility, via leverage effect or other channels.
8:249:20924:20:21:79:533:320:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We model the contemporaneous relation between country-specific GDP growth and stock market
8:250:21014:21:20:79:533:299:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:volatility.  We argue that one can think of GDP as the ‘dividend’ or the ‘cash flow’ associated
8:251:21109:20:20:79:533:279:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:with the country stock market index.  In this sense,  the novelty of our modeling approach is
8:252:21202:20:21:79:533:259:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to  work  in  the  dividend-volatility  (or  cash  flow-volatility)  space  rather  than  return-volatility
8:253:21309:21:20:79:533:238:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:space.  Indeed, our identification strategy exploits the fact that country-specific dividend growth
8:254:21408:20:20:79:533:218:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:processes (the country GDP growth rates) are less correlated across countries as compared to
8:255:21500:20:24:79:314:198:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the cross-market correlation of equity volatilities.
8:256:21552:24:20:96:533:174:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The rest of the paper is organized as follows.  Section 2 sets out the theoretical multi-country
8:257:21648:20:20:79:533:154:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:model and derives country-specific equity returns and volatilities and shows how they are re-
8:258:21741:20:21:79:533:134:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:lated to the underlying world technology factor and its higher moments.  Section 3 considers
8:259:21833:21:20:79:533:113:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the econometric issues involved in identification of the real and financial factors using a static
8:260:21931:20:20:79:533:93:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:version of our econometric multi-country model.  Section 4 extends the analysis to a dynamic
8:261:22023:20:0:79:533:73:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:setting.  Section 5 considers the use of realized volatility as a proxy measure for uncertainty in
9:262:22122:0:21:79:533:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:a multi-country setting.  Section 6 reports key stylized facts of the data, including evidence on
9:263:22219:21:20:79:533:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the cross-country correlation structure of volatilities and output growth.  Section 7 reports the
9:264:22316:20:20:79:533:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:main empirical results of the paper on the comparison between unconditional and conditional
9:265:22407:20:21:79:533:648:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:correlations between volatility and growth.  Section 8 reports forecast error variance decompo-
9:266:22502:21:20:79:533:627:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:sitions and discusses the corresponding empirical results.  Section 9 presents impulse responses,
9:267:22599:20:20:79:533:607:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and Section 10 concludes.  Some of the technical proofs and details of the data and their sources
9:268:22696:20:21:79:533:587:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:are provided in the Appendix.  Derivation of impulse responses and variance decompositions,
9:269:22787:21:20:79:533:566:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:together with additional empirical results as well as selected country-specific results are reported
9:270:22887:20:23:79:296:546:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:in a separate online supplement to the paper.
9:271:22932:23:21:96:532:523:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f4:Notations:Letw= (w1,w2,...,wn)′andA= (aij) be ann×1 vector and ann×nmatrix,

9:283:23702:20:46:79:175:340:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and Pesaran (2013).
9:284:23721:46:27:79:533:294:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:2    Equity  Returns  and  Volatility  in  a  Multi-country  Business
9:285:23790:27:34:103:192:267:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:Cycle Model
9:286:23801:34:20:79:533:233:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:In  this  section  we  set  up  a  simple  theoretical  model  of  the  business  cycle  with  time-varying
9:287:23908:20:21:79:533:213:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:volatility that will help to guide the empirical analysis.  To this end we consider a multi-country

9:289:24103:20:20:79:533:172:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:link between changes in volatility and business cycle fluctuations via a common (global) risk-free
9:290:24201:20:21:79:532:152:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:rate. Specifically, consider a world consisting ofNeconomies (countries) indexed byi= 1,2,...N,

9:293:24480:20:0:79:533:91:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to a world growth factor, assumed to be exogenously given.  The world growth factor is largely,
10:294:24576:0:24:79:324:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:but not exclusively, driven by technological factors.

17:784:37161:20:20:79:532:416:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f13:order moments of shocks.  The presence of these higher order terms,  however,  inducesstrong
17:785:37253:20:21:79:533:396:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:cross sectional dependence (in the sense to be made precise in the following section) in country
17:786:37349:21:20:79:533:375:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:realized volatilities even if the effects of the growth innovation,νt, onritandσ2itare eliminated.
17:787:37447:20:20:79:533:355:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:In the next section,  we will exploit the difference in the degree of cross sectional dependence
17:788:37543:20:21:79:533:335:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of the country output growth rates and realized volatilities, after controlling for the effects of
17:789:37641:21:20:79:533:314:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the common growth factor shock,νt,  to identify such innovations from the data,  and we will
17:790:37733:20:20:79:533:294:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:combine all higher order terms in a single common financial shock.  In practice, one would expect
17:791:37830:20:20:79:533:274:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:additional factors such as market imperfections, speculative bubbles and other forms of financial
17:792:37927:20:21:79:533:254:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:frictions to influence realized equity market volatilities.  We therefore view our theoretical model
17:793:38027:21:20:79:533:233:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:more as a benchmark providing insights for the empirical analysis that follows, rather than a
17:794:38120:20:46:79:237:213:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:true characterization of the data.
17:795:38154:46:34:79:448:167:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:3    A Static Multi-Country Econometric Framework
17:796:38203:34:21:79:533:133:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We  now  build  on  the  theoretical  insights  that  underlie  the  growth  and  volatility  equations,
17:797:38307:21:20:79:533:112:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(1)  and  (27),  and  develop  a  suitable  multi-country  econometric  framework  for  the  empirical
17:798:38409:20:20:79:533:92:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:analysis of cross country and time variations of the relations between growth and volatility.  We
17:799:38506:20:0:79:533:72:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:begin with a static specification, omitting dynamics and deterministic components to simplify
18:800:38601:0:21:79:533:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the  exposition.   We  also  start  by  positing  the  following  single  unobservable  common  factor
18:801:38703:21:37:79:147:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:representation
18:802:38717:37:23:265:532:651:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f4:vit=λift+uit,(28)
18:803:38734:23:37:256:532:628:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:∆yit=γift+εit,(29)
18:804:38752:37:20:79:532:591:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:fori= 1,2,...,N;t= 1,2,...,T, where as before ∆yitis real GDP growth,18andvit= ln(σit) is
18:805:38841:20:23:79:531:571:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the log of realized stock market volatility for countryiduring periodt(measured in quarters).
18:806:38934:23:20:96:533:548:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The common factor representation in (28)-(29) is general and motivated by both empirical
18:807:39022:20:21:79:533:528:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:evidence and standard economic theory.  From an empirical perspective, as noted in the intro-
18:808:39115:21:20:79:533:507:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:duction, realized equity price volatility and output growth share a large and negative contempo-
18:809:39211:20:20:79:533:487:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:raneous correlation at the country level, for most countries in our sample.  This correlation is a
18:810:39309:20:21:79:533:467:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:robust stylized fact of the data documented also by Baker and Bloom (2013), Carriere-Swallow
18:811:39401:21:20:79:533:446:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and Cespedes (2013), and Nakamura et al. (2017).  From a theoretical perspective, as shown in
18:812:39494:20:20:79:533:426:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the previous section, one can think offtas a common world growth factor (e.g., technology),
18:813:39585:20:21:79:533:406:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:which affects all countries GDP growth rates and equity price volatilities contemporaneously,
18:814:39678:21:20:79:533:385:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:which we will call ‘real’ factor in the rest of the paper.  In view of our theoretical derivations in
18:815:39779:20:20:79:532:365:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the previous section,ftcould be viewed as a pure ‘level’ or ‘first moment’ factor in the sense of
18:816:39876:20:23:79:226:345:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Gorodnichenko and Ng (2017).
18:817:39904:23:21:96:533:322:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:It is worth noting that without further restrictions on the cross section correlations ofuitand
18:818:39999:21:20:79:532:301:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f4:εit, it is not possible to be sure about the number of common factors affecting output growth and
18:819:40096:20:20:79:532:281:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:volatility.  In our theoretical derivations, we assumeεitto be cross sectionally weakly dependent
18:820:40193:20:21:79:533:261:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and deriveuitin terms of level and higher-order moments offt.  It follows that most likelyεitand
18:821:40289:21:20:79:532:240:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f4:uitwill be correlated, and due to the remaining common component affectinguit, it is also likely
18:822:40385:20:20:79:532:220:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:thatuitwill be cross sectionally strongly correlated.  This interpretation is also in the spirit of
18:823:40484:20:21:79:533:200:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the Arbitrage Pricing Theory of Ross (1976) and Chamberlain and Rothschild (1982) applied to
18:824:40576:21:20:79:532:179:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:second moments.19In our empirical application we will find that whileftis sufficient to render
18:825:40670:20:20:79:532:159:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the cross-country correlations ofεitto be weak (required in our theoretical derivations), we need
18:826:40767:20:21:79:532:139:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:at least one more common factor to span the cross-country correlations of theuit, which we saw
18:827:40861:21:16:79:532:118:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:in the previous section can be affected by higher order moments of ∆yit.  In the paper, we will
18:828:40956:16:11:87:353:102:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:18We also refer to ∆yitas ‘output growth’ or ‘growth’ for brevity.
18:829:41022:11:0:87:365:91:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:19See, for example, Herskovic et al. (2016) and Renault et al. (2016).
19:830:41094:0:24:79:528:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:refer to this second factor as “financial” and interpret it as a combined higher moment factor.
19:831:41189:24:20:96:533:685:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:This econometric specification is not tied to any particular asset price model, but incorpo-
19:832:41281:20:20:79:533:665:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:rates two practically relevant features:  time-varying volatility and heterogeneity in the form of
19:833:41379:20:21:79:533:645:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:country-specific loadings on the common factors.  There are also dynamic features that need to
19:834:41473:21:20:79:533:624:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:be taken into account that vary across countries due to geographical location, institutions, and
19:835:41569:20:39:79:458:604:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:history.  We will consider heterogeneous dynamics across countries in Section 4.
19:836:41649:39:30:79:269:565:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:3.1    Identifying the Real Factor

20:886:43346:31:21:79:532:546:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f13:Assumption 3(Cross-country correlations) The country-specific innovations,uitandεit, have
20:887:43435:21:20:79:533:525:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:zero  means  and  finite  variances,  and  are  serially  uncorrelated,  but  can  be  correlated  with  each
20:888:43544:20:20:79:533:505:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:other both within and between countries.  Furthermore, denoting the variance-covariance matrices
20:889:43640:20:21:79:532:485:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f4:of  theN×1innovation  vectorsεt=  (ε1t,ε2t,...,εNt)′andut=  (u1t,u2t,...,uNt)′byΣεε=
20:890:43724:21:37:79:377:464:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f13:V ar(εt)andΣuu=V ar(ut), respectively, it is assumed that:
20:891:43782:37:23:252:532:427:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f4:%max(Σu)   =O(N),(35)
20:892:43803:23:39:253:532:404:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f4:%max(Σε)   =O(1).(36)
20:893:43824:39:21:96:533:365:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Assumption 1 is standard in the factor literature (see, for instance, Assumption B in Bai and
20:894:43917:21:20:79:533:344:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Ng (2002)).  It ensures thatftis a strong (or pervasive) factor for both volatility and growth
20:895:44011:20:20:79:533:324:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:so that it can be estimated consistently either using principal components or by cross-section
20:896:44105:20:24:79:395:304:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:averages of country-specific observations (see Chudik et al., 2011).
20:897:44173:24:20:96:533:280:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Assumption  2  requires  that  individual  countries’  contribution  to  world  growth  or  world
20:898:44270:20:20:79:532:260:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:volatility is of order 1/N.  This is consistent with the notion that,  since the 1990s,  when our
20:899:44367:20:21:79:533:240:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:sample period starts, world growth and world capital markets have become progressively more
20:900:44458:21:23:79:389:219:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:diversified and integrated as a result of the globalization process.
20:901:44526:23:20:96:533:196:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The first part of Assumption 3 is also standard and leaves the causal relation between the
20:902:44616:20:20:79:533:176:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:idiosyncratic components,uitandεit, unrestricted. In our model, the correlation betweenuitand
20:903:44709:20:21:79:532:156:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f4:εitcaptures any contemporaneous causal relation between country-specific volatility and growth,
20:904:44804:21:23:79:532:135:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:conditional onft, on which we do not impose any restrictions for the purpose of identifyingft.
20:905:44898:23:20:96:532:112:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The second part of Assumption 3 is crucial to identifyftas the following proposition demon-
20:906:44989:20:20:79:533:92:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:strates.   The  assumption  states  that  the  volatility  innovations  are  strongly  correlated  across
20:907:45094:20:0:79:533:72:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:countries, while growth innovations are weakly correlated across countries.  Weak cross-country
21:908:45191:0:21:79:532:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:correlation in turn means that, asymptotically, asNbecomes large, the average pair-wise cor-
21:909:45283:21:20:79:533:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:relations  across  countries  of  growth  innovations  tends  to  zero,  since  the  largest  eigenvalue  of
21:910:45391:20:20:79:533:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:their variance-covariance matrix is bounded inN.20On the other hand, strong cross-country
21:911:45480:20:21:79:533:648:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:correlation means that the average pair-wise correlation of volatility innovations does not tend
21:912:45576:21:20:79:533:627:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to zero because the largest eigenvalue ofΣugrows with the size of the cross-section,N.  As we
21:913:45669:20:20:79:533:607:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:shall see, this key assumption is in accordance not only with the empirical properties of the data
21:914:45767:20:21:79:533:587:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:displayed in Figure 2, but also with the properties of the innovations that we obtain from the
21:915:45861:21:29:79:172:566:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:model estimation.21

22:959:47106:35:20:79:532:638:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f13:Remark 1(Estimation  offt)  Asftis  pervasive  or  strong,  we  can  estimate  it  with  either  as

22:962:47371:35:21:96:533:563:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Indeed, Figure S.2 in the online supplement shows that the first (static) principal component
22:963:47464:21:20:79:532:542:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and the cross section average of ∆yitprovide estimates offtthat are very close, with a correlation
22:964:47562:20:20:79:532:522:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of 0.9.  In the present context the use  of the cross-section-average (CSA) estimator offthas
22:965:47655:20:21:79:533:502:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:two  advantages.   First,  it  can  be  directly  interpreted  as  global  GDP  growth.   Second,  under
22:966:47759:21:20:79:532:481:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Assumptions  1  and  3  the  CSA  estimator  offtis  consistent  so  long  asNis  large,  whilst  the
22:967:47860:20:20:79:533:461:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:principal component estimator requires bothNandTto be large (See section 19.5.1 of Pesaran
22:968:47950:20:36:79:117:441:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(2015)).
22:969:47958:36:20:79:532:405:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f13:Remark 2(Principal component on the panel of volatility series) The cross-section average or
22:970:48050:20:35:79:462:385:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:the principal component of the panel of volatilities seriesvitdoes not identifyft.
22:971:48132:35:20:96:533:350:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:This is because the volatility innovations,uit, are assumed to be strongly correlated across

22:974:48410:20:20:79:533:289:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to zero.  Under Assumption 3, only the principal component or cross-section average of output
22:975:48503:20:35:79:240:269:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:growth can be used to identifyft.

22:982:49050:20:20:79:532:97:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:component extracted from the panel ofvitand ∆yitcaptures a linear combination offtand any
22:983:49139:20:0:79:411:77:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:additional common factors that exclusively affect the volatility series.
23:984:49213:0:21:96:532:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f6:Before concluding this discussion, it is worth noting that, whilst theoretically we needN→

23:986:49394:20:20:79:533:668:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f4:N→∞, is best viewed as a counterfactual that considers the extent to which the strength of the
23:987:49488:20:21:79:533:648:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:connections among units declines withN.  In our experience, working with many cross-country
23:988:49579:21:39:79:300:627:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:panels,Naround 30 is often sufficiently large.
23:989:49625:39:30:79:297:588:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:3.2    Identifying the Financial Factor
23:990:49664:30:20:79:533:558:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The main empirical result of the paper does not require explicit identification of the additional
23:991:49761:20:21:79:532:538:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:strong factors assumed to be exclusive to the volatilities,vit.  But doing so permits exploring
23:992:49856:21:20:79:533:517:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:other  properties  of  the  data  that  underpin  the  second  and  the  third  main  empirical  results
23:993:49960:20:20:79:533:497:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:summarized above.  With this in mind, recall that, under condition (35) of Assumption 3, the

23:995:50156:21:20:79:533:456:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:factor that is not shared by the growth innovations.  By assuming, without loss of generality,

23:997:50342:20:21:79:533:416:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:orthonormal transformation of the factor loadings in the country-specific volatility equations.
23:998:50437:21:20:79:533:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A formal statement of this result is provided in Proposition 2 below and established under the

24:1048:52636:20:21:79:533:217:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:series is filtered out.  It is not a pure second-moment factor factor in the sense of Gorodnichenko

25:1056:53321:0:31:79:512:709:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:3.3    Consistent Estimation of Orthogonalized Real and Financial Factors

25:1069:54362:20:33:79:349:399:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:toft, without requiring additional economic restrictions.

26:1136:55399:0:12:361:377:614:11:g_d0_f21:8:g_d0_f19:∑T

26:1141:55495:23:20:96:532:562:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Proposition  3  accomplishes  two  objectives.   It  derives  an  observable  proxy  forgtand  it
26:1142:55592:20:20:79:533:542:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:makes sure that the resultant estimator is orthogonal to the proxy forft, which will turn out
26:1143:55685:20:21:79:533:522:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to  be  useful  when  we  estimate  error  variance  decompositions  and  impulse  responses.   This  is
26:1144:55789:21:20:79:532:501:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:achieved simply by choosing coefficients for the linear combination of  ̄vω,ton ∆ ̄yω,tsuch that the
26:1145:55889:20:35:79:529:481:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:observable common factors have zero-means, unit variance and are orthogonal to each other.23
26:1146:55981:35:21:79:532:446:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f13:Remark 4(World  economy  as  a  single-country  model  versus  a  multi-country  representation)
26:1147:56077:21:20:79:533:425:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:Model (28)-(29) applies to allNcountries.  Consider a generic countryi,  like for instance the
26:1148:56171:20:20:79:533:405:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:United States,  or a closed system like the whole world economy.  If we focus on one country in
26:1149:56266:20:21:79:533:385:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:isolation from the rest of the world, or consider a single country global model, we cannot identify
26:1150:56365:21:20:79:532:364:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:the  parameters  of  (28)-(29),  even  assuming  that  the  innovationsuitandεitare  orthogonal  to
26:1151:56464:20:35:79:459:344:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f13:each other andftis known, unless we excludeftfrom one of the two equations.
26:1152:56539:35:43:96:436:309:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:To see this, note that the covariance matrix ofvitand ∆yitis given by:
26:1153:56609:43:0:229:252:266:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Θi=
26:1154:56612:0:19:256:266:288:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f21:
26:1155:56613:19:0:256:276:269:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f7:λ
26:1156:56615:0:7:277:281:280:8:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f5:2
26:1157:56616:7:18:277:351:273:8:g_d0_f19:8:g_d0_f19:i+σ2u,iλiγi
26:1158:56627:18:0:281:362:255:11:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f19:λiγiγ2i+σ2ε,i
26:1159:56640:0:19:367:377:288:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f21:
26:1160:56641:19:46:367:532:269:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f4:.(51)
26:1161:56647:46:20:79:532:223:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:This provides three independent restrictions, but (28)-(29) contains four free parameters, (λi,γi),
26:1162:56746:20:20:79:533:203:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and (σ2u,i,σ2ε,i).  Identification of the model parameters requires at least oneadditionalrestriction
26:1163:56847:20:21:79:533:183:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:at the country level–for instance,λi= 0 orγi= 0, even if it is assumed that innovationsuitand
26:1164:56940:21:16:79:233:162:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f4:εitare orthogonal to each other.
26:1165:56972:16:14:87:532:146:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:22These mean corrections will be applied automatically if intercepts are included in the country-specific models
26:1166:57084:14:8:79:135:132:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:(46) and (47).
26:1167:57098:8:14:87:532:124:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:23In the present static set up,ζtcorresponds to the growth factor shockνtintroduced in Section 2; butξtneed
26:1168:57205:14:11:79:532:110:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:not correspond directly to the growth factor volatility innovations,χt, also defined in Section 2.  This is because
26:1169:57320:11:0:79:490:99:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:realized volatilities could also be affected by other factors besides growth factor volatility innovations.
27:1170:57429:0:21:96:533:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:To summarize, the key feature of our identification strategy lies in the fact that no restric-
27:1171:57523:21:20:79:533:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:tion  is  imposed  at  the  individual  country  level.   Restrictions  apply  only  to  the  cross-section
27:1172:57630:20:20:79:533:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:correlations of a large number of countries under consideration.  Specifically, we propose a novel
27:1173:57728:20:21:79:533:648:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:approach  that  exploits  the  differences  in  the  degree  of  cross-country  correlations  for  the  two
27:1174:57835:21:20:79:533:627:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:series of innovations.  The growth innovations are assumed to be cross-sectionally weakly cor-
27:1175:57929:20:20:79:533:607:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:related, while the volatility innovations are assumed cross-sectionally strongly correlated.  As a
27:1176:58027:20:21:79:532:587:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:result,  the effect of country-specific growth innovations on the global variable ∆ ̄yω,tvanish if
27:1177:58125:21:20:79:533:566:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f4:Nis reasonably large, while the effects of the country-specific volatility innovations on  ̄vω,tdo
27:1178:58223:20:20:79:533:546:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:not vanish even if the cross section dimension is large.  Under these assumptions the matrix of
27:1179:58318:20:21:79:533:526:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:contemporaneous factor loadings is recursive, which enables us to obtain consistent estimates of
27:1180:58414:21:20:79:533:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the common orthogonal real and financial factors from the data simply by means of OLS, as in
27:1181:58506:20:20:79:532:485:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f19:a Cholesky decomposition of the variance-covariance matrix of ∆ ̄yω,tand   ̄vω,t, ordering ∆ ̄yω,t
27:1182:58604:20:21:79:533:465:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:first.  Importantly, however, our identification assumptions are not consistent with an alternative
27:1183:58703:21:20:79:533:444:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:ordering of the factors in the Cholesky decomposition where  ̄vω,tis included first.  Furthermore,
27:1184:58801:20:20:79:533:424:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:our  strategy  does  not  apply  to  a  single  country,  or  to  the  world  economy  viewed  as  a  single
27:1185:58909:20:21:79:533:404:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:closed-system.  The identification strategy used here is general and can be applied to any panel
27:1186:59005:21:20:79:533:383:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of time series with the necessary cross-section correlation properties.  With this approach, we
27:1187:59100:20:20:79:533:363:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:can identify more factors provided that we consider more cross sections of variables with the
27:1188:59193:20:21:79:533:343:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:appropriate structure of correlation across countries.  What is crucial is to adopt a multi-country
27:1189:59292:21:20:79:533:322:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:approach covering a large number of countries, as opposed to considering single country models
27:1190:59386:20:46:79:135:302:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:in isolation.
27:1191:59399:46:34:79:451:256:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:4    A Dynamic Multi-Country Heterogeneous Model
27:1192:59447:34:20:79:533:222:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Whilst the static model considered so far is helpful for illustrative purposes, in empirical appli-
27:1193:59546:20:21:79:533:202:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:cations it is important to take dynamics, possibly differing across countries, into account.  As we
27:1194:59645:21:20:79:533:181:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:shall see, allowing for dynamics that differ across countries, while requiring additional regularity
27:1195:59745:20:23:79:361:161:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:conditions and derivations, does not alter our main results.
27:1196:59805:23:37:96:499:138:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Consider the following first-order dynamic version of the static model (46) and (47):
27:1197:59890:37:23:173:532:101:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f4:vit=aiv+φi,11vi,t−1+φi,12∆yi,t−1+λift+θigt+ηit,(52)
27:1198:59941:23:0:164:532:78:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:∆yit=aiy+φi,21vi,t−1+φi,22∆yi,t−1+γift+εit.(53)
28:1199:59990:0:37:79:212:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:In matrix notation we have:

28:1202:60100:43:0:89:110:592:11:g_d0_f18:11:g_d0_f4:ai=

31:1368:66377:20:20:79:533:489:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:results, but before doing so we need to discuss how we measure volatility in our multi-country
31:1369:66471:20:46:79:114:469:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:setting.
31:1370:66479:46:34:79:269:423:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:5    Volatility Measurement
31:1371:66506:34:21:79:533:389:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:As a proxy for uncertainty we use realized equity price volatility.  Realized volatility has been
31:1372:66603:21:20:79:533:368:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:used extensively in the theoretical and empirical finance literature and implicitly assumes that
31:1373:66699:20:20:79:532:348:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:uncertainty and risk can be characterized in terms of probability distributions.26Specifically,
31:1374:66794:20:21:79:533:328:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:we use a measure of quarterly realized volatility based on the summation of daily squared stock
31:1375:66889:21:20:79:533:307:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:price returns.  This is a natural application of within-day measures of volatility based on high
31:1376:66985:20:23:79:257:287:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:frequency within-day price changes.27
31:1377:67022:23:20:96:532:264:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Denote the daily equity price of countryi, measured at close of dayτin quartertasPit(τ).
31:1378:67110:20:40:79:384:244:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The realized volatility for countryiin quartertis computed as:
31:1379:67172:40:0:251:275:204:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f4:σ2it=
31:1380:67177:0:27:281:295:218:8:g_d0_f19:11:g_d0_f21:Dt∑
31:1381:67180:27:0:279:294:191:8:g_d0_f19:8:g_d0_f5:τ=1
31:1382:67183:0:42:296:532:204:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(rit(τ)− ̄rit)2(64)
31:1383:67202:42:0:79:270:162:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f19:whererit(τ) = ∆ lnPit(τ), and  ̄rit=D−1t
31:1384:67242:0:11:280:301:170:11:g_d0_f21:6:g_d0_f15:∑Dt
31:1385:67245:11:17:292:532:159:8:g_d0_f19:11:g_d0_f4:τ=1rit(τ) is the average daily price changes in the
31:1386:67296:17:16:79:533:142:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:quartert, andDtis the number of trading days in quartert.  Note that we have now divided
31:1387:67384:16:15:87:532:126:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:25We  describe  how  we  can  compute  the  relative  importance  of  these  factors  for  the  forecast  error  variance
31:1388:67505:15:11:79:533:111:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:decomposition of country-specific variables, and the impulse response function of the country specific variables to
31:1389:67620:11:7:79:287:100:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:these shocks in the online supplement to the paper.
31:1390:67671:7:11:87:505:93:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:26It therefore abstracts from Knightian uncertainty, where one cannot attach probabilities to outcomes.
31:1391:67774:11:0:87:472:82:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:27See, for example, Andersen et al. (2001, 2003), Barndorff-Nielsen and Shephard (2002, 2004))
32:1392:67870:0:21:79:533:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the right hand side of (64) byDtso that our measure of realized volatility is consistent with
32:1393:67963:21:20:79:532:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:quarterly GDP growth.  Note that, for most time periods,Dt= 3×22 = 66, which is larger
32:1394:68049:20:20:79:533:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:than  the  number  of  data  points  typically  used  in  the  construction  of  daily  realized  market
32:1395:68153:20:21:79:533:648:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:volatility in the empirical finance literature.28Finally, note that, because variances have right-
32:1396:68251:21:20:79:533:627:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:skewed distributions, but logarithmic variances tend to have near Gaussian distributions, in our
32:1397:68347:20:20:79:533:607:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:empirical application we will be working with the logarithm of realized volatility measures, i.e.
32:1398:68444:20:24:79:144:587:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f7:vit= log(σit).
32:1399:68458:24:20:96:533:563:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The realized volatility of asset prices is not the only way of measuring ‘risk’ or ‘uncertainty’.
32:1400:68555:20:20:79:533:543:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:If we consider a panel of country equities (e.g., of firms or sectorswithina country), a different
32:1401:68653:20:21:79:533:523:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:measure of uncertainty can be computed as the cross-sectional dispersion of equity prices within
32:1402:68749:21:20:79:533:502:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:each  country.   In  Section  S1  of  the  online  supplement  we  show  that,  under  fairly  general  as-
32:1403:68856:20:20:79:532:482:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:sumptions, and forDtrelatively large (as in our sample), the cross-sectional dispersion of equity
32:1404:68953:20:21:79:532:462:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:returns within countryiis closely related to the realized volatility of the country equity returns.
32:1405:69052:21:23:79:504:441:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:So, in our application, we will focus on the realized volatility of country equity indexes.29
32:1406:69145:23:20:96:533:418:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Realized  volatility  and  cross-sectional  dispersion  encompass  most  measures  of  uncertainty
32:1407:69243:20:20:79:533:398:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and risk proposed in the literature that could be used to implement our identification strategy.
32:1408:69339:20:21:79:533:378:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Schwert (1989b), Ramey and Ramey (1995), Bloom (2009), Fernandez-Villaverde et al. (2011)
32:1409:69428:21:20:79:533:357:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:use aggregate time series volatility (i.e.,  summary measures of dispersion over time of output
32:1410:69523:20:20:79:533:337:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:growth,  stock  market  returns,  or  interest  rates);  Leahy  and  Whited  (1996),  Campbell  et  al.
32:1411:69626:20:21:79:533:317:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(2001),  Bloom  et  al.  (2007)  and  Gilchrist  et  al.  (2013)  use  dispersion  measures  at  the  firm-
32:1412:69733:21:20:79:533:296:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:level stock market returns; Bloom et al. (2012) use cross-sectional dispersion of plant, firm, and
32:1413:69831:20:23:79:327:276:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:industry profits, stocks, or total factor productivity.
32:1414:69886:23:20:96:533:253:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:In the finance literature, the focus of the volatility measurement has now shifted to implied
32:1415:69979:20:21:79:533:233:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:volatility measures obtained from option prices, like the US VIX Index (see for example Berger
32:1416:70073:21:20:79:533:212:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:et  al.,  2017).   However,  a  key  input  for  the  implementation  of  our  identification  strategy  is
32:1417:70180:20:20:79:533:192:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the availability of country-specific measures of uncertainty for a large number of countries over
32:1418:70277:20:21:79:533:172:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:a  long  period  of  time,  and  implied  volatility  measures  are  not  yet  available  for  a  meaningful
32:1419:70385:21:16:79:533:151:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:number of countries.30The literature has also used uncertainty measures based on expectations
32:1420:70478:16:14:87:532:135:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:28In the case of intra-day observations, for example, prices are usually sampled at 10-minutes intervals which
32:1421:70588:14:8:79:323:121:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:yield around 48 intra-daily returns in an 8-hour trading day.
32:1422:70649:8:11:87:532:113:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:29Daily returns are computed abstracting from dividends, which are negligible by comparison to price changes.
32:1423:70758:11:14:87:532:102:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:30Figure S.5 in the supplement plots the US realized volatility measure we constructed with the VIX index during
32:1424:70870:14:11:79:533:88:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:the period over which they overlap and shows that the two measures co-move very closely with a correlation of
32:1425:70979:11:0:79:119:77:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:about 0.9.
33:1426:70991:0:21:79:532:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:dispersion.31While the measure proposed by Rossi and Sekhposyan (2015) is available for a
33:1427:71080:21:20:79:533:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:large number of countries, the time series dimension is unbalanced and often not long enough
33:1428:71172:20:20:79:533:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:for  our  purposes.   Finally,  model  based  measures,  such  as  those  in  Jurado  et  al.  (2015)  and
33:1429:71278:20:21:79:533:648:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Ludvigson et al. (2015) could in principle be computed for all countries in our sample, but the
33:1430:71373:21:20:79:533:627:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:data requirements to construct such measures for many countries over a sufficiently long time
33:1431:71466:20:46:79:186:607:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:period are prohibitive.
33:1432:71489:46:34:79:521:561:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:6    Data and Selected Stylized Facts for Volatility and Growth
33:1433:71552:34:20:79:533:527:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:This  section  briefly  describes  the  data  set  we  use  in  the  empirical  analysis  and  reports  some
33:1434:71660:20:20:79:533:507:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:stylized  facts  based  on  the  unconditional  moments  of  the  data.   Specifically,  we  consider  the
33:1435:71766:20:21:79:533:487:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:degree of persistence in the growth and volatility series, that is relevant for our model specifi-
33:1436:71864:21:20:79:533:466:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:cation; and examine the patterns of cross-country correlations, which play an important role in
33:1437:71959:20:23:79:205:446:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:our identification strategy.
33:1438:71987:23:20:96:533:423:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The  sources  of  the  data  and  their  sampling  information  are  reported  in  Appendix  B.  To
33:1439:72086:20:21:79:533:403:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:construct a balanced panel for the largest number of countries for which we have sufficiently
33:1440:72179:21:20:79:533:382:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:long time series, we first collect daily stock prices for 32 advanced and emerging economies from
33:1441:72276:20:20:79:533:362:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:1979 to 2011.  We then cut the beginning of the sample in 1993, as daily equity price data are
33:1442:72370:20:21:79:533:342:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:not available earlier for two large emerging economies (Brazil and China) and for Peru.  Better
33:1443:72465:21:20:79:533:321:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:quality quarterly GDP data for China also became available from 1993.  Our results seem to be
33:1444:72558:20:20:79:533:301:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:robust to excluding these three countries and starting the sample in 1988.  Moreover, some steps
33:1445:72654:20:21:79:532:281:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of the empirical analysis, like the estimator of factor innovations (ˆζtandˆξt), can be implemented
33:1446:72753:21:38:79:533:260:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:with the unbalanced panel from 1979 without any significant consequence for our main findings.
33:1447:72847:38:30:79:175:222:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:6.1    Persistence
33:1448:72865:30:21:79:533:192:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:A  battery  of  summary  statistics  on  the  realized  volatility  series  and  the  real  GDP  series  (in
33:1449:72973:21:20:79:533:171:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:levels) supports our model specification in terms of the log-level of realized volatility and the
33:1450:73070:20:20:79:533:151:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:log-differences of real GDP. As Table S.1 in the online supplement shows, the levels of realized
33:1451:73166:20:21:79:533:131:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:volatility, even though persistent, tend to be mean-reverting.  Table S.2 in the supplement shows
33:1452:73263:21:20:79:532:110:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:that the first order auto-correlation coefficient for realized volatility is on average about 0.6. Also
33:1453:73366:20:15:79:533:90:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:standard ADF tests reject the null hypothesis of unit roots in the volatility series.  In contrast,
33:1454:73465:15:0:87:507:75:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:31See, for instance, Zarnowitz and Lambros (1987), Popescu and Smets (2010), Bachmann et al. (2013).
34:1455:73567:0:21:79:532:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the persistence of real GDP levels is very high (on average around 0.99).  Moreover, the null of
34:1456:73663:21:20:79:533:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:a unit root for the level of log-GDP cannot be rejected by standard ADF tests for any of the 32
34:1457:73758:20:39:79:193:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:countries in our sample.
34:1458:73782:39:30:79:269:629:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:6.2    Cross-country Correlations
34:1459:73815:30:21:79:532:599:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f13:The differential pattern of cross-country correlations of the growth and volatilityinnovations
34:1460:73909:21:20:79:532:578:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f13:is crucial for our identification strategy.  Here we consider the properties of the observedtime
34:1461:74005:20:20:79:532:558:11:g_d0_f13:11:g_d0_f4:seriesas  displayed  in  Figure  2.   In  order  to  gauge  the  extent  to  which  volatility  and  growth
34:1462:74112:20:21:79:533:538:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:series co-move across countries, we use two techniques:  standard principal component analysis
34:1463:74206:21:23:79:320:517:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and pair-wise correlation analysis across countries.
34:1464:74258:23:20:96:532:494:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:In a panel of countries indexed byi= 1,2,...,N, the average pair-wise correlation of country

34:1466:74452:20:21:79:532:454:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:countriesj(i.e., for allj6=i).  The average pair-wise correlationacrossall countries, denoted
