34:1511:75102:7:13:306:317:176:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f21:√
34:1512:75103:13:0:316:344:163:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f19:1 +  ̃γ2j
34:1513:75112:0:19:347:357:197:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f21:
34:1514:75113:19:0:347:357:178:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f21:
34:1515:75114:0:20:357:361:195:8:g_d0_f5:8:g_d0_f5:2
34:1516:75115:20:0:364:372:175:11:g_d0_f6:11:g_d0_f6:−
34:1517:75116:0:15:388:393:183:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:1
34:1518:75117:15:0:376:404:168:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f4:N−1
34:1519:75120:0:43:406:409:175:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f7:.
34:1520:75121:43:21:79:108:132:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Hence
34:1521:75126:21:0:272:308:111:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f7: ̄ρN=O
34:1522:75132:0:9:310:315:120:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f21:(
34:1523:75133:9:0:316:329:111:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f19: ̄γ2N
34:1524:75138:0:9:330:335:120:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f21:)
34:1525:75139:9:30:336:532:111:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f4:,(66)
34:1526:75144:30:0:79:160:81:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:where  ̄γN=N−1
34:1527:75158:0:11:162:181:89:11:g_d0_f21:8:g_d0_f19:∑N
34:1528:75160:11:0:174:444:78:8:g_d0_f19:11:g_d0_f4:i=1 ̃γimeasures the degree of pervasiveness of the factor.
35:1529:75220:0:21:96:532:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The  attraction  of  the  average  pair-wise  correlation,   ̄ρN,  lies  in  the  fact  that  it  applies  to
35:1530:75329:21:20:79:533:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:multi-factor processes, and unlike factor analysis does not require the factors to be strong.  In
35:1531:75426:20:20:79:532:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:fact, the average pair-wise correlation,  ̄ρN, tends to be a strictly positive number if ∆yitcontains
35:1532:75527:20:21:79:532:648:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:at least one strong factor, otherwise it tends to zero asN→∞.  Therefore, non-zero estimates
35:1533:75619:21:20:79:533:627:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of  ̄ρNare suggestive of strong cross-sectional dependence.32For completeness, and to show that
35:1534:75714:20:20:79:533:607:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:our analysis is robust to using an alternative methodology, in what follows, we also use standard
35:1535:75811:20:24:79:228:587:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:principal component analysis.33
35:1536:75842:24:20:96:533:563:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Country-specific average pair-wise correlations of volatility and GDP growth are reported
35:1537:75931:20:20:79:533:543:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:in Figure 2.  Recall that the average pair-wise correlation across all countries for the realized
35:1538:76028:20:21:79:533:523:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:volatility series is 0.56.  In contrast, the average pair-wise correlation across all countries for the
35:1539:76131:21:20:79:533:502:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:growth series at 0.27 is much smaller.  As we can see, the pair-wise correlations of volatility and
35:1540:76230:20:20:79:533:482:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:growth have a similar values for different countries, but there is a clear difference between the
35:1541:76327:20:21:79:533:462:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:two variables.  This suggests that both variables may share at least one strong common factor,
35:1542:76421:21:23:79:517:441:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:even though volatilities seem to co-move more across countries than the GDP growth rates.
35:1543:76510:23:20:96:533:418:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Principal  component  analysis  yields  similar  results.   The  first  principal  component  in  our
35:1544:76611:20:20:79:533:398:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:panel  of  realized  volatility  series  explains  65  percent  of  the  total  variation  in  the  log-level  of
35:1545:76724:20:21:79:533:378:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:volatility, whilst the first principal component of the growth series accounts for only around 30
35:1546:76821:21:20:79:533:357:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:percent  of  total  cross-country  variations.   Thus,  both  in  the  case  of  the  pair-wise  correlation
35:1547:76929:20:20:79:533:337:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and principal component analysis, the results point to a much higher degree of cross-country co-
35:1548:77025:20:21:79:533:317:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:movements for the volatility series than for the growth series. As we will see, these differences are
35:1549:77126:21:20:79:533:296:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:even more pronounced in the case of the estimated innovations series obtained using equations
35:1550:77219:20:46:79:146:276:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(62) and (63).
35:1551:77233:46:34:79:489:230:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:7    Estimated Common and Country-specific Components
35:1552:77286:34:20:79:533:196:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The preliminary analysis above is compatible with the common factor model proposed in the pa-
35:1553:77379:20:21:79:533:176:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:per, suggesting a stronger degree of cross-country co-movements for volatility series as compared
35:1554:77476:21:20:79:533:155:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to the growth series.  The summary statistics reported also support the model specification in
35:1555:77570:20:20:79:533:135:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:terms of log-level of volatility and log-difference of growth.  Now we will use our multi-country
35:1556:77667:20:17:79:533:115:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:factor-augmented  VAR  model,  (62)  and  (63),  to  interpret  the  observed  negative  association
35:1557:77767:17:15:87:532:98:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:32Formal  tests  of  cross-sectional  dependence  based  on  estimates  of   ̄ρNare  discussed  in  Pesaran  (2015)  and
35:1558:77887:15:7:79:304:83:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:reported, for our panel of countries, in the next section.
35:1559:77945:7:0:87:252:76:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:33See also Chapter 29 in Pesaran (2015).
36:1560:77987:0:24:79:224:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:between volatility and growth.
36:1561:78017:24:20:96:532:685:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We begin by estimating the global factor innovations,ˆζtandˆξt, using (60) and (61).  We then
36:1562:78110:20:20:79:533:665:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:estimate country-specific VAR models conditional on these innovations and obtain estimates of
36:1563:78203:20:21:79:532:645:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the country-specific growth and volatility innovations,εitandηit.  The necessary computations
36:1564:78296:21:20:79:532:624:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:are carried out by applying OLS to (62)-(63) for eachiseparately.  Finally, we compute and re-
36:1565:78390:20:20:79:532:604:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:portconditionalpair-wise correlations across countries for country-specific volatility and growth
36:1566:78487:20:21:79:533:584:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:innovations to evaluate our identification assumptions, and within-country correlations between
36:1567:78582:21:20:79:533:563:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:volatility  and  growth  innovations  to  assess  the  model’s  ability  to  capture  the  countercyclical
36:1568:78688:20:20:79:533:543:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:nature of realized volatility.  It is important to note that we will also estimate country-specific
36:1569:78787:20:21:79:532:523:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:volatility innovations,uit, by conditioning only onˆζtrather than both onˆζtandˆξtin (62)-(63).
36:1570:78882:21:20:79:533:502:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Thus, we will present results for estimated values of bothηitanduitas the latter are derived
36:1571:78974:20:39:79:207:482:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:under weaker assumptions.
36:1572:78999:39:30:79:372:443:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:7.1    Estimated Global Real and Financial Shocks
36:1573:79048:30:20:79:533:413:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The global shocks,ˆζtandˆξt, are recovered from the OLS estimation of (60) and (61).  Figure
36:1574:79140:20:21:79:533:393:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:3 plots them when estimated using the unbalanced panel from 1979 (thin lines with asterisks),
36:1575:79233:21:20:79:533:372:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and when we use the balanced panel from 1993 (thick solid lines), so as to better illustrate their
36:1576:79331:20:20:79:533:352:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:time profiles.  The figure also reports one-standard deviation bands for the shocks.  Note that
36:1577:79426:20:21:79:533:332:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the shocks are standardized and have zero means and unit in-sample variances.  They are also
36:1578:79518:21:23:79:321:311:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:serially uncorrelated and orthogonal to each other.
36:1579:79569:23:20:96:533:288:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The figure shows that the largest common real shock was after the second oil shock in 1979,
36:1580:79660:20:21:79:533:268:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and during the fourth quarter of 2008 after the Lehman’s collapse.  Also note that, after a very
36:1581:79756:21:20:79:533:247:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:large positive shock in the second quarter of 2009, the size of the subsequent impulses declines
36:1582:79852:20:20:79:533:227:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:persistently, which is consistent with the anemic global recovery experienced in the aftermath
36:1583:79946:20:18:79:533:207:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of the global financial crisis.  The sizes of largest absolute values of common financial shocks,
36:1584:80043:18:23:79:533:189:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:ˆξtcoincide with the 1987 stock market crash and the 2008 Lehman’s collapse.  Our estimates
36:1585:80134:23:20:79:533:166:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of global financial shocks co-move positively, but not closely, with the US measures of financial
36:1586:80231:20:20:79:532:146:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:volatility, risk and investor sentiment.  In general,ˆξtseries is more volatile and by construction
36:1587:80330:20:21:79:532:126:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:less persistent as compared to the these (raw) US measures.  The correlation ofˆξtwith the US
36:1588:80423:21:0:79:532:105:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Baa-Treasury credit spread and Excess Bond Premium of Gilchrist and Zakrajsek (2012) is 0.20

38:1626:82431:39:30:79:490:588:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:7.2    Cross-country Correlations of Volatility and Growth Innovations
38:1627:82501:30:20:79:533:558:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Although the restrictions behind our identification assumptions cannot be formally tested, our
38:1628:82595:20:21:79:533:538:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:multi-country  approach  permits  us  to  investigate  the  extent  to  which  the  implications  of  the
38:1629:82700:21:20:79:532:517:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:identified model are in line with the identification restrictions made.35To this end, we explore
38:1630:82796:20:20:79:533:497:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the cross-country correlations of the estimated residuals from the dynamic regressions (62) and
38:1631:82891:20:23:79:418:477:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:(63), with and without conditioning on the financial shocks series,ˆξt.36
38:1632:82964:23:21:96:533:454:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Panel A of Figure 4 plots, for each country in our sample, the average pair-wise correlation
38:1633:83056:21:17:79:533:433:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of the volatility innovations (ˆuit) and the growth innovations (ˆεit), when we condition only on
38:1634:83153:17:21:79:533:416:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:ˆζtin model (62)-(63).  Panel B reports the same statistics when we condition on bothˆζtand
38:1635:83244:21:23:79:532:395:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:ˆξtin model (62)-(63).37The statistics reported are the same as in Figure 2.  The blue (darker)
38:1636:83339:23:20:79:532:372:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:bars are the average pair-wise correlations of the country-specific growth innovations (ˆεit).  The
38:1637:83438:20:23:79:532:352:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:yellow (lighter) bars are for the country-specific volatility innovations (ˆuitand ˆηit, respectively).
38:1638:83541:23:21:96:532:329:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Panel A of Figure 4 shows that, if we condition only onˆζtin (62)-(63), the volatility inno-
38:1639:83633:21:20:79:533:308:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:vations display average pair-wise correlations comparable to those of the data reported for all
38:1640:83728:20:20:79:533:288:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:countries in Figure 2.  In contrast, the pair-wise correlations of the growth innovations are neg-
38:1641:83826:20:21:79:532:268:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:ligible, with an average across all countries of 0.03.38Panel B of Figure 4 also shows that, if we
38:1642:83924:21:20:79:533:247:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:condition on bothˆζtandˆξt, the cross-country correlations of the volatility innovations are now
38:1643:84020:20:20:79:533:227:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:negligible, as in the case of the growth innovations, with an average pair-wise correlation across
38:1644:84118:20:20:79:533:207:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:all countries equal to 0.02.  For instance, in the specific case of the US, the average pair-wise
38:1645:84215:20:21:79:532:187:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:correlation of the volatility innovations is equal to 0.6 conditioning onˆζtalone.  But it drops
38:1646:84311:21:16:79:532:166:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to−0.05 if we condition on both factor innovations.  By comparison, the US average pair-wise
38:1647:84403:16:15:87:532:150:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:35Note that we can estimateζtandξtconsistently by means of the OLS regressions (60) and (61) only under the
38:1648:84510:15:10:79:533:135:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:identification assumptions made.  As a result, whilst we can directly estimate pair-wise correlations of volatility
38:1649:84625:10:11:79:533:125:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:and growth series, we can not examine cross-country pair-wise correlations of their innovations without imposing
38:1650:84737:11:9:79:202:114:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:these identification conditions.
38:1651:84769:9:10:87:460:105:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:36Recall that, in this case, we run OLS on (62) without conditioning onˆξtin the regression.

39:1674:86169:23:20:96:532:223:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Figure 4, therefore, illustrates that after conditioning onˆζt—which is common to both growth
39:1675:86262:20:21:79:533:203:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and volatility series—not much commonality is left in the case of growth innovations, but the
39:1676:86355:21:20:79:532:182:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f19:volatility innovations share additional strong factors.  Moreover, after conditioning on bothˆζt
39:1677:86451:20:20:79:532:162:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:andˆξt, the volatility innovations also appear weakly correlated because of the near-zero average
39:1678:86548:20:20:79:533:142:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:pair-wise  correlation  across  all  countries,  thus  suggesting  thatonlytwo  common  shocks  are
39:1679:86647:20:21:79:533:122:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:necessary to span their correlations across-countries as we assume.  It is, therefore, interesting
39:1680:86745:21:20:79:532:101:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f13:to test whether the two sets of innovations also satisfy a formal definition ofweakandstrong
39:1681:86837:20:0:79:283:81:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:dependence, as we assumed deriving them.
40:1682:86879:0:21:96:533:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:To test for  weak  and  strong cross-section dependence,  we  estimate  the  cross-sectional  de-
40:1683:86976:21:20:79:533:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:pendence (CD) test statistic of Pesaran (2015) and the exponent of cross sectional dependence
40:1684:87069:20:20:79:532:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(α) proposed in Bailey et al. (2016).  The CD statistic is normally distributed with zero-mean
40:1685:87163:20:21:79:533:648:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and unit-variance under the null of zero average pair-wise correlations.  So,  the critical value
40:1686:87260:21:20:79:533:627:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:is  around  2.   When  the  null  is  rejected,  Bailey  et  al.  (2016)  suggest  estimating  the  strength
40:1687:87368:20:20:79:532:607:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of the cross-section dependence with an exponent, denotedαin the range (1/2,1], with unity
40:1688:87458:20:21:79:532:587:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:giving the maximum degree of cross dependence. Any value above 1/2 and below 1, but signifi-
40:1689:87550:21:20:79:533:566:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:cantly different from 1, suggests weak dependence.39So, in what follows, we present estimates
40:1690:87643:20:20:79:532:546:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:ofαfor the volatility and the growth innovations, together with their confidence intervals.  For
40:1691:87739:20:21:79:532:526:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:comparison, we also report the same estimates for the (raw) growth (∆yit) and volatility (vit)
40:1692:87833:21:20:79:108:505:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:series.

43:1767:93533:21:23:79:273:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:such a common factor from the analysis.
43:1768:93572:23:20:96:533:665:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:How  can  we  interpret  this  evidence?   While  we  are  agnostic  on  which  specific  structural
43:1769:93672:20:21:79:533:645:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:model may or may not generate the pattern of cross-country correlations that we have assumed
43:1770:93764:21:20:79:533:624:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:in our identification strategy and documented above, given our theoretical model, it is reasonable
43:1771:93862:20:20:79:532:604:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to interpret the common growth innovations,ˆζt, as reflecting variations in the global risk free
43:1772:93958:20:21:79:533:584:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:rate.  Specifically, in Section 2.1 and 2.2, using a simple multi-country model, we showed that
43:1773:94053:21:20:79:533:563:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:expected world growth is tied to the world risk-free rate, and changes in expected world growth
43:1774:94148:20:20:79:533:543:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:can affect both country volatilities and country growth rates at the same time.  Lower expected
43:1775:94243:20:21:79:533:523:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:world growth means a lower world risk-free rate, and hence higher country risk premium and
43:1776:94333:21:20:79:533:502:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:country  volatility,  but  also  lower  country  growth.   Our  real  common  factor,  therefore,  drives
43:1777:94438:20:23:79:149:482:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:both variables.
43:1778:94453:23:20:96:533:459:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Note, however, that the evidence reported above does not imply that changes in volatility
43:1779:94542:20:21:79:532:439:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:over  time  are  mostly  driven  byˆζt.   That  is,  while  these  shocks  can  account  for  most  of  the
43:1780:94649:21:20:79:533:418:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:contemporaneous co-movement between volatility and growth, they do not necessarily explain
43:1781:94739:20:20:79:533:398:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:a significant share of the observed time variations in global innovations to volatility.  Indeed, as
43:1782:94839:20:21:79:533:378:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:we will see in the next section,ˆζtexplains a relatively small share of the variation of volatility
43:1783:94938:21:46:79:328:357:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:over time, with a much larger share explained byˆξt.
43:1784:94990:46:27:79:533:311:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:8    Volatility  and  Growth  Forecast  Error  Variance  Decomposi-
43:1785:95057:27:34:103:137:284:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:tions
43:1786:95062:34:20:79:533:250:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Forecast error variance decompositions are routinely used to quantify the importance of a given
43:1787:95157:20:20:79:533:230:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:shock for the time-variation of the endogenous variables at different time horizons, relative to
43:1788:95253:20:21:79:533:210:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:other shocks in the model.  Our factor augmented multi-country VAR model can be readily used
43:1789:95345:21:20:79:533:189:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to decompose the forecast error variance of country volatility and growth in terms of the common
43:1790:95441:20:20:79:532:169:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:shocks,ˆζtandˆξt, as well as the 64 vector of country-specific shocks, ˆηitand ˆεitfori= 1,2,....,32.
43:1791:95542:20:21:79:532:149:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:While the global real and financial shocks,ˆζtandˆξt, are orthogonal to the country-specific shocks
43:1792:95641:21:20:79:532:128:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and to each other by construction, the country-specific shocks ˆηitand ˆεitare left unrestricted,
43:1793:95738:20:20:79:532:108:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and can be correlated,  both within and between countries,  even conditional onˆζtandˆξt.  In
43:1794:95831:20:0:79:533:88:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:order to compute and interpret forecast error variance decompositions, we therefore have to deal
44:1795:95929:0:24:79:325:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:with this source of within country interdependence.
44:1796:95980:24:20:96:533:685:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Consider first the correlation between volatility and growth innovations within each country.
44:1797:96073:20:20:79:532:665:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f19:We saw in Figure 5 that the contemporaneous within-country correlation between  ˆηitand ˆεit
44:1798:96165:20:21:79:533:645:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:is very small and not statistically significant for all but two emerging market economies, once
44:1799:96260:21:20:79:533:624:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:we condition on the global shocksˆζtandˆξt.  Nonetheless, even assuming the estimated reduced
44:1800:96353:20:20:79:532:604:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f19:form covariance matrix were truly diagonal, this would not imply that innovations ˆηitand ˆεit
44:1801:96447:20:21:79:533:584:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:can  be  interpreted  as  ‘structural’  country-specific  volatility  and  growth  shocks.   As  it  is  well
44:1802:96556:21:20:79:532:563:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:known there always exists an orthonormal transformation of ˆηitand ˆεitthat lead to the same
44:1803:96648:20:23:79:260:543:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:forecast error variance decomposition.
44:1804:96686:23:20:96:532:520:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:It is, therefore, important that the 64×64 matrix of correlations among all 32 countries and
44:1805:96778:20:21:79:533:500:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:both variables is considered in a full multi-country set up.  Our results show that, conditional
44:1806:96874:21:20:79:532:479:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f19:on both real and financial common shocks,ˆζtandˆξt, the country-specific innovations ˆεitand ˆηit
44:1807:96971:20:20:79:533:459:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:are weakly correlated across countries (Figure 4).  The average pair-wise correlations of volatility
44:1808:97071:20:21:79:532:439:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and growth is negligible, and even in the case of China and India they were well below 0.2.  As we
44:1809:97169:21:20:79:532:418:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:discussed above, weak cross-sectional dependence means that, asNgrows, the overall average
44:1810:97259:20:20:79:533:398:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:pair-wise  correlation  tends  to  zero.  This  further  means  that,  while  some  pairs  of  correlations
44:1811:97366:20:21:79:533:378:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:can be different from zero, not all pairs can be so.  In practice, this means that most correlation
44:1812:97465:21:23:79:431:357:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:pairs will be very small and the overall covariance matrix must be sparse.
44:1813:97539:23:20:96:533:334:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We exploit the sparsity of the correlation matrix of country-specific shocks by making al-
44:1814:97629:20:20:79:533:314:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:ternative  assumptions regarding  the causal  relations  between the  country-specific  innovations
44:1815:97728:20:21:79:532:294:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:ˆηitand ˆεit, and show that the inference we draw is reasonably robust to different estimates of
44:1816:97824:21:20:79:533:273:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the country-specific error correlation matrix.  As a first approximation, we assume that the only
44:1817:97921:20:20:79:533:253:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:source of interdependence among all growth and volatility series are the global real and financial
44:1818:98019:20:21:79:532:233:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:shocksˆζtandˆξt.  This implies assuming that country-specific volatility and growth shocks have
44:1819:98114:21:20:79:533:212:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:no contemporaneous impact on growth or volatility series within and across countries.  Despite
44:1820:98208:20:20:79:533:192:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:its  apparent  severity,  this  assumption  seems  justified  by  our  empirical  finding  that  there  ex-
44:1821:98315:20:21:79:533:172:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:ist very limited conditional within-country correlations and weak cross-country correlations as
44:1822:98410:21:23:79:170:151:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:summarized above.
44:1823:98427:23:20:96:533:128:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We then check the robustness of the results from this ‘benchmark’ scenario, by comparing
44:1824:98515:20:21:79:533:108:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:them with those obtained under weaker assumptions.  While maintaining the assumption of zero
44:1825:98607:21:0:79:533:87:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:conditional correlations between countries, we assume that country-specific volatility shocks can
45:1826:98706:0:21:79:533:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:have a contemporaneous causal impact on growth variables but notvice-versa, in line with much
45:1827:98799:21:20:79:533:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of the existing empirical literature as reviewed in the Introduction.  This is done by allowing for
45:1828:98898:20:20:79:533:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:a block-diagonal error covariance matrix in the full multi-country model, in which the only non-
45:1829:98994:20:21:79:533:648:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:zero off-diagonal elements are the estimated covariances between volatility and growth errors of
45:1830:99090:21:20:79:533:627:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:each country block.  These within-country blocks are factorized with a Cholesky decomposition,
45:1831:99184:20:23:79:237:607:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:ordering volatility before growth.
45:1832:99218:23:21:96:533:584:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Finally, as a third possibility we refrain altogether from interpreting country-specific volatil-
45:1833:99315:21:20:79:533:563:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:ity  and  growth  shocks  as  structural,  and  make  use  of  a  general  unrestricted  error  covariance
45:1834:99421:20:20:79:533:543:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:matrix  subject  to  the  sparsity  condition,  both  within  and  across  countries  and  compute  the
45:1835:99524:20:21:79:533:523:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:generalized forecast error variance decompositions (GFEVD) of Pesaran and Shin (1998), rather
45:1836:99617:21:20:79:533:502:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:than orthogonal forecast error variance decompositions that require Cholesky ordering of the
45:1837:99709:20:20:79:533:482:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:shocks.  However, before computing GFEVDs, we use the regularized multiple testing threshold
45:1838:99801:20:21:79:533:462:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:estimator of the error covariance matrix proposed by Bailey et al. (2017) and described in more
45:1839:99896:21:20:79:533:441:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:detail below, to obtain a consistent estimator of the 64×64 error covariance matrix for the full
45:1840:99992:20:20:79:533:421:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:multi-country model.  This regularized estimator exploits the sparsity of the underlying error
45:1841:100086:20:23:79:167:401:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:covariance matrix.
45:1842:100104:23:21:96:533:378:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:In what follows we report results for these three alternative specifications of the covariance
45:1843:100198:21:20:79:532:357:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:matrix of the innovations ˆεitand ˆηit.  As we wish to quantify the relative importance of both the
45:1844:100297:20:17:79:533:337:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:real and the financial common shocks, all results are based on (62)-(63) that include bothˆζtand
45:1845:100393:17:24:79:533:320:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:ˆξt.  Specifically, Figure 6 reports the forecast error variance decompositions (FEVDs) obtained
45:1846:100489:24:20:79:533:296:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:assuming the 64×64 error covariance matrix is diagonal; Figure 7 reports the results obtained for
45:1847:100586:20:20:79:533:276:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:a block-diagonal error covariance matrix and a Cholesky decomposition within each block; and
45:1848:100678:20:21:79:533:256:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Figure 8 reports the generalized FEVDs (GFEVDs) obtained using the regularized estimator
45:1849:100766:21:20:79:533:235:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of  the  error  covariance  matrix.41Each  figure  reports  the  ‘average’  variance  decomposition,
45:1850:100866:20:20:79:533:215:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:weighting  country-specific  decompositions  with  PPP-GDP  weights.   We  shall  now  summarize
45:1851:100962:20:39:79:500:195:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the error variance decompositions that result from these three alternative specifications.
45:1852:101052:39:30:79:464:156:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:8.1    Diagonal Covariance Matrix and Orthogonal Decomposition
45:1853:101114:30:21:79:533:126:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The  left  hand  panel  of  Figure  6  plots  the  average  forecast  error  variance  decomposition  of
45:1854:101218:21:16:79:533:105:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:volatility  across  all  countries  in  our  sample  under  a  diagonal  error  covariance  matrix.   The
45:1855:101323:16:0:87:530:89:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:41The derivation of the FEVDs and GFEVDs is reported in section S3 of the online supplement to the paper.
46:1856:101430:0:21:79:533:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:figure shows that country volatility is driven largely by common financial shocks (blue area with
46:1857:101527:21:20:79:533:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:vertical lines) and country-specific volatility shocks (red area with crosses).  Combined together,
46:1858:101626:20:20:79:533:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:these two shocks explain about 95 percent of the total variance of realized volatility over time.
46:1859:101723:20:21:79:533:648:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Real common shocks (purple area with diagonal lines) explain less than 5 percent of the total
46:1860:101816:21:20:79:533:627:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:volatility forecast error variance.  Country growth shocks, as well as all other 31 country-specific
46:1861:101916:20:20:79:533:607:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:foreign growth shocks in the full model, play essentially no role.  These results, therefore, suggest
46:1862:102017:20:21:79:533:587:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:that country volatility is largely driven by global financial shocks and its own country-specific
46:1863:102114:21:20:79:533:566:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:innovations.  In other words, according to these results, the component of volatility driven by
46:1864:102209:20:20:79:533:546:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:common or country-specific output shocks, and hence the ‘endogenous’ component of country-
46:1865:102299:20:36:79:412:526:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:specific volatility in the sense of Ludvigson et al. (2015) is very small.

46:1885:102651:11:0:81:355:250:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:lines); ˆηiis country-specific volatility shock (red area with crosses);
46:1886:102723:0:7:358:368:257:9:g_d0_f27:9:g_d0_f27:∑

46:1890:102962:0:7:438:448:233:9:g_d0_f27:9:g_d0_f27:∑

46:1893:103093:11:31:81:152:204:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:1993:Q1-2011:Q2.
46:1894:103109:31:20:96:533:173:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:It  is  worth  noting  that  these  estimated  shares  of  the  forecast  error  variance  of  volatility
46:1895:103214:20:21:79:533:153:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:are similar to the central estimates of Ludvigson et al. (2015) for the US. In that study,  the
46:1896:103309:21:20:79:533:132:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:share of macroeconomic shocks in the forecast error variance of financial volatility is estimated
46:1897:103406:20:20:79:533:112:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:at just above 5 percent in the long run.  However, while Ludvigson et al. (2015) attribute this
46:1898:103501:20:20:79:533:92:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to the US business cycle (as proxied by a shock to US industrial production),  we attribute a
46:1899:103594:20:0:79:533:72:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:similar outcome to the global real shock, which can be interpreted as an international business
47:1900:103691:0:21:79:533:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:cycle factor, and find that country-specific growth shocks have little or no explanatory power
47:1901:103785:21:23:79:226:688:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:for country-specific volatility.42
47:1902:103819:23:20:96:533:665:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Consider now the forecast error variance decomposition of GDP growth reported on the right
47:1903:103909:20:21:79:533:645:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:hand side of Figure 6.  The figure shows that, on average, the forecast error variance of country
47:1904:104006:21:20:79:533:624:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:specific GDP growth is driven mostly by country-specific growth shocks and global real shocks,
47:1905:104100:20:20:79:533:604:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:with a combined share approaching 90 percent of the total in the long run (green areas with
47:1906:104191:20:21:79:533:584:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:squares and purple area with diagonal lines, respectively).  The country-specific growth shock
47:1907:104285:21:20:79:533:563:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:explains more than 60 percent of the total forecast error variance in the long-run, while the real
47:1908:104383:20:20:79:533:543:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:global shock on average explains around 30 percent of the total growth forecast error variance.
47:1909:104478:20:21:79:533:523:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:This is in line with existing results in the international business cycle literature (see, for instance,
47:1910:104582:21:23:79:179:502:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:Kose et al. (2003)).43
47:1911:104604:23:20:96:533:479:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Global financial shocks explain about 8-10 percent of country-specific growth forecast error
47:1912:104696:20:20:79:533:459:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:variance, on average, in our sample.  The importance of these shocks picks up gradually over the
47:1913:104792:20:21:79:533:439:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:forecast horizon and stabilizes within two years.  In contrast, the own country-specific volatility
47:1914:104891:21:20:79:533:418:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:shock, explains only a small share of the total forecast error variance of GDP growth, with a
47:1915:104984:20:20:79:532:398:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:weight of about 1−2 percent, while the combination of all other 31 country-specific volatility
47:1916:105078:20:21:79:533:378:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:shocks in the model explain only a small share of country growth variance.  These results clearly
47:1917:105175:21:20:79:533:357:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:illustrate the quantitative importance of distinguishing between common and country-specific
47:1918:105267:20:39:79:159:337:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:volatility shocks.
47:1919:105285:39:30:79:501:298:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:8.2    Block-Diagonal Covariance Matrix and Orthogonal Decomposition
47:1920:105353:30:21:79:533:268:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We  now  maintain  the  assumption  of  zero  correlations  of  country-specific  shocks  (after  condi-
47:1921:105457:21:20:79:533:247:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:tioning on the common shocks) across countries, but allow for a possibly non-zero correlation
47:1922:105550:20:20:79:533:227:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:between volatility and growth within each country.  Specifically, we assume that, at the coun-
47:1923:105644:20:20:79:533:207:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:try level, a volatility shock can affect growth within a quarter but notvice  versa.  This is the
47:1924:105741:20:16:79:533:187:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:assumption typically made in the empirical literature on volatility and the business cycle.  So,
47:1925:105837:16:15:87:532:171:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:42Results  for  specific  countries,  including  the  United  States,  are  reported  in  the  online  supplement.   As  can
47:1926:105961:15:11:79:533:156:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:be seen from Figures S.6 to S.9 also in the online Supplement, countries behave pretty similarly, with some but
47:1927:106072:11:11:79:533:145:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:limited heterogeneity.  The results for the United States, in particular, are similar to those for the average economy
47:1928:106190:11:7:79:136:134:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:reported here.
47:1929:106204:7:15:87:532:127:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:43Notice that these results imply that countries’ business cycles remain largely unexplained within our econo-
47:1930:106314:15:11:79:533:112:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:metric model.  Indeed, in the data, there are many shocks at work, and this is captured in our relatively simple
47:1931:106426:11:11:79:533:101:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:empirical framework by the large share of growth forecast error variance accounted for by the own country specific
47:1932:106540:11:0:79:139:90:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:growth shocks.
48:1933:106556:0:21:79:533:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:here, we are ‘identifying’ exogenous country-specific volatility changes with a Cholesky decom-
48:1934:106651:21:20:79:533:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:position of the within-country covariance matrix.  We do so by ordering volatility first in the
48:1935:106746:20:36:79:157:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:model (62)-(63).

48:1964:107599:32:20:96:533:314:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The results for this specification are given in Figure 7 and can be seen to be virtually identical
48:1965:107697:20:20:79:533:294:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to the estimates obtained for the diagonal error covariance matrix reported in Figure 6.  This
48:1966:107791:20:21:79:533:274:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:is perhaps not surprising given that the correlations between the country-specific innovations,
48:1967:107886:21:39:79:469:253:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:once the effects of the common shocks are removed, are very small as in Figure 5.
48:1968:107967:39:21:79:533:214:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:8.3    Thresholding the Error Covariance Matrix and Generalized Decomposi-
48:1969:108041:21:30:109:132:193:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:tion
48:1970:108045:30:20:79:532:163:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We  finally  allow  for  a  fully  estimated  (64×64)  correlation  matrix,  both  within  and  across
48:1971:108147:20:20:79:533:143:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:countries, and compute the GFEVDs.  However, given the large size of this matrix, we regularize
48:1972:108242:20:21:79:533:123:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:it by computing a threshold estimator following Bailey et al. (2017), who developed a procedure
48:1973:108337:21:20:79:533:102:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:based on results from the multiple testing literature.  Specifically, we first test for the statistical
48:1974:108440:20:0:79:533:82:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:significance of each of the 2016 distinct off-diagonal elements of the (64×64) matrix.  We then
49:1975:108537:0:21:79:533:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:set to zero all those elements that are not statistically significant, using suitably adjusted critical
49:1976:108640:21:20:79:533:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:values to allow for the large number of tests that are being carried out.  We then finally compute
49:1977:108738:20:23:79:533:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the GVEDs by using the regularized estimates as derived in the online supplement to the paper.
49:1978:108832:23:21:96:533:645:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Table 2 below lists all the non-zero correlation pairs.  As can be seen, only 50 out of 2016
49:1979:108924:21:20:79:533:624:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:total off-diagonal elements are statistically different from zero. Of these, about half are positively
49:1980:109026:20:20:79:533:604:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:correlated and the other half are negatively correlated, with an average value that is close to
49:1981:109121:20:21:79:533:584:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:zero.  Most notably, there is no surviving within-country contemporaneous correlation between
49:1982:109214:21:20:79:533:563:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:volatility and growth, except for India.  There are also very few significant GDP-GDP correlation
49:1983:109311:20:20:79:532:543:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:pairs  (i.e.,  ˆεitwith ˆεjt),  with  no  obvious  regional  pattern  of  co-movements.   There  are  a  few
49:1984:109419:20:21:79:532:523:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:significant pairs of volatility-volatility correlations (i.e., ˆηitwith ˆηjt), but involving only a handful
49:1985:109526:21:20:79:533:502:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of countries, with no evidence of a dominant role for the United States.  Finally, there are a few
49:1986:109624:20:20:79:533:482:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:significant GDP-volatility correlation pairs (i.e., ˆεjtwith ˆηit) for a few countries, like Belgium,
49:1987:109725:20:23:79:453:462:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:China, France, Italy and the Netherlands, again revealing no specific patterns.
49:1988:109804:23:21:96:533:439:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The  estimated  generalized  forecast  error  variance  decompositions  (GFEVDs),  reported  in
49:1989:109899:21:20:79:533:418:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Figure  8,  are  consistent  with  those  obtained  assuming  a  diagonal  or  block-diagonal  error  co-
49:1990:110004:20:20:79:532:398:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:variance matrix.44Relative to the results with diagonal or block-diagonal covariance matrix in
49:1991:110098:20:0:79:504:378:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Figures  6  and  7,  the  contribution  of  foreign  country-specific  volatility  (growth)  shocks,
49:1992:110198:0:8:509:521:386:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f21:∑
49:1993:110199:8:21:522:531:378:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f19:ˆηj
49:1994:110202:21:0:79:83:357:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(
49:1995:110203:0:9:83:95:366:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f21:∑
49:1996:110204:9:20:96:533:357:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:ˆεj), to domestic volatility (growth) is now larger, but the spillover effects of foreign volatility
49:1997:110304:20:20:79:533:337:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:shocks to growth (and foreign growth shocks to volatility) remain negligible.  Moreover, global
49:1998:110399:20:21:79:533:317:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:financial shocks and domestic country-specific volatility shocks continue to explain the bulk of
49:1999:110495:21:20:79:533:296:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the forecast error variance of volatility.  Similarly,  real global shocks and the country-specific
49:2000:110594:20:201:79:458:276:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:growth shocks remain the main drivers of the forecast error variance of growth.
49:2001:110673:201:0:87:496:75:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:44Notice here that the GFEVDs need not to sum to 100 as the underlying shocks are not orthogonal.

51:2093:113967:56:34:79:490:237:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:9    The Transmission of Global Real and Financial Shocks
51:2094:114024:34:20:79:533:203:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The  last  step  of  our  empirical  analysis  is  the  computation  of  impulse  responses  of  country-
51:2095:114129:20:21:79:533:183:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:specific volatility and growth to global real and financial shocks,ˆζtandˆξt.  While forecast error
51:2096:114228:21:20:79:533:162:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:variance decompositions speak to the importance of a particular shock for the time-variation
51:2097:114320:20:20:79:533:142:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of  the  endogenous  variables  relative  to  other  shocks  in  the  model,  impulse  responses  provide
51:2098:114425:20:20:79:533:122:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:information on the size of the effects of the shocks and their transmission across variables and
51:2099:114521:20:24:79:125:102:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:countries.
51:2100:114531:24:0:96:533:78:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Figure 9 displays a weighted average of the country-specific impulse responses using PPP-
52:2101:114622:0:21:79:533:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:GDP weights (solid line), together with two-standard deviation error bands (shaded areas).  The
52:2102:114717:21:20:79:531:688:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:error bands are computed based on the dispersion of the impulse responses across countries.45
52:2103:114810:20:20:79:532:668:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f19:We focus on the effects of positive unit (one-standard deviation) real and financial shocks,ˆζt
52:2104:114905:20:36:79:120:648:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:andˆξt.46

52:2131:115132:118:11:84:526:338:9:g_d0_f9:9:g_d0_f11:Note.  Average impulse responses to one-standard deviation real and financial shocks,ˆζtandˆξt.  The solid
52:2132:115238:11:11:84:526:327:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:lines  are  the  PPP-GDP  weighted  averages  of  the  country-specific  responses.   The  shaded  areas  are  the  two
52:2133:115357:11:11:84:526:316:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:standard deviations confidence intervals.  See equations (S3.12) and (S3.13) for the derivations and Figure S.12
52:2134:115469:11:32:84:360:305:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:for the country-specific responses.  Sample period:  1993:Q1-2011:Q2.
52:2135:115538:32:20:96:533:273:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Panels  (A)  and  (B)  of  Figure  9  display  the  average  across  countries  of  the  volatility  and
52:2136:115642:20:20:79:533:253:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:growth responses to a real global shock.  These figures show that a positive real global shock
52:2137:115736:20:21:79:533:233:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:increases output growth and lowers volatility.  This reflects an endogenous volatility response
52:2138:115831:21:20:79:533:212:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:to the fundamental improvements in the world economy.  Note that the error bands around the
52:2139:115922:20:20:79:533:192:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:average responses are very tight, reflecting relatively homogeneous country responses.  In fact, as
52:2140:116021:20:21:79:533:172:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:can be seen from Figure S.12, provided in the online supplement, the impulse responses have a
52:2141:116114:21:20:79:533:151:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:similar shape for most countries.  The average impact of this shock on country volatilities is one
52:2142:116212:20:16:79:533:131:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:order of magnitude smaller than its impact on country output growth, but it is quite persistent,
52:2143:116308:16:15:87:532:115:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:45The derivation of the average impulse response functions to common factor shocks and their error bands is
52:2144:116415:15:11:79:533:100:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:provided in the online supplement S3, equations (S3.12) and (S3.13).  The estimated country-specific responses
52:2145:116525:11:7:79:458:89:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:to the two common shocks are reported in Figure S.12 in the online Supplement to the paper.
52:2146:116616:7:0:87:527:82:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:46Recall that these shocks are orthogonal to all other shocks in the model and to each other by construction.
53:2147:116727:0:21:79:533:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:taking more than three years for the effects of the shocks to vanish completely.  Panel (B) also
53:2148:116823:21:20:79:532:688:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:shows that, on average, country growth loads positively onˆζt, with persistent effects up to 8-10
53:2149:116920:20:20:79:533:668:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:quarters, as one would expect.  Country output growth increase by about half a percentage point
53:2150:117015:20:21:79:532:648:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:following a one-standard error change inˆζt.  This is consistent with the existing evidence on the
53:2151:117113:21:20:79:533:627:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:international business cycle,  which attributes an important role to a world factor, along with
53:2152:117208:20:23:79:516:607:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:regional and country-specific factors, in driving the business cycle (e.g., Kose et al. (2003)).
53:2153:117304:23:21:96:533:584:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Panels (C) and (D) of Figure 9 report the responses of volatility and growth to a positive
53:2154:117394:21:20:79:532:563:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:global financial shock,ˆξt.  These average responses suggest that a positive shock toˆξtis ‘bad
53:2155:117489:20:20:79:533:543:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:news’ for the world economy,  as volatility increases and growth declines.  For a one-standard
53:2156:117583:20:21:79:533:523:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:deviation  shock  to  the  common  financial  factor,  volatility  increases  by  25  basis  points,  while
53:2157:117690:21:20:79:533:502:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:growth  declines  by  about  15  basis  points  within  two  quarters  after  the  shock.47Although
53:2158:117789:20:20:79:533:482:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:smaller  than  the  growth  response  to  the  real  common  factor  shock  in  panel  B,  the  average
53:2159:117892:20:21:79:533:462:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:growth response to the global financial shock in panel D is of the same order of magnitude, and
53:2160:117987:21:20:79:533:441:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:hence quantitatively sizable.  The average responses to the common financial shock are also very
53:2161:118083:20:20:79:533:421:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:persistent, but there is much more heterogeneity in the country growth responses, as can be seen
53:2162:118179:20:20:79:533:401:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:from Figure S.12 provided in the online supplement.  Therefore, these impulse responses suggest
53:2163:118274:20:21:79:533:381:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:that, even though common financial shocks may not explain a very large share of the forecast
53:2164:118366:21:23:79:533:360:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:error variance of output growth over time, they can cause large and persistent global recessions.
53:2165:118463:23:20:96:533:337:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Impulse responses to country-specific shocks have qualitatively similar pattern of transmis-
53:2166:118555:20:21:79:533:317:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:sion but, as one would expect given the forecast error variance results, are quantitatively much
53:2167:118651:21:23:79:289:296:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:smaller than responses to common shocks.48
53:2168:118693:23:20:96:533:273:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:The pattern of shock transmissions in Figure 9 is consistent with country volatility increasing
53:2169:118788:20:20:79:533:253:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:in response to the large declines in the world output in the second part of 2008, and the world
53:2170:118883:20:21:79:533:233:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:recession being amplified by the exceptionally large common financial shock in the fourth quarter
53:2171:118980:21:20:79:533:212:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of 2008, and the first quarter of 2009.  The transmission in Figure 9 can also help in explaining
53:2172:119077:20:20:79:533:192:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the seemingly puzzling coexistence of high policy volatility (as in Baker et al. (2016)) and low
53:2173:119173:20:21:79:533:172:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:equity market volatility after the beginning of the Trump administration with a combination of
53:2174:119267:21:16:79:357:151:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:a real and a financial shock partially offsetting each other.
53:2175:119328:16:14:87:532:135:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:47Note that the delayed growth response to the global financial shock follows from our identification assumptions,
53:2176:119442:14:8:79:310:121:9:g_d0_f11:9:g_d0_f11:but it is not imposed directly on country-specific models.
53:2177:119500:8:0:87:376:113:6:g_d0_f12:9:g_d0_f11:48These are not reported but are available from the authors on request.
54:2178:119573:0:34:79:195:709:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:10    Conclusions
54:2179:119590:34:21:79:533:675:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Empirical measures of uncertainty behave countercyclically in most countries of the world, but
54:2180:119684:21:20:79:533:654:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:economic theory suggests that causation can run both ways.  In this paper,  we study the in-
54:2181:119776:20:20:79:533:634:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f13:terrelation between realized equity price volatility and GDP growth without imposinga priori
54:2182:119868:20:21:79:533:614:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:restrictions on the direction of economic causation.  We develop a multi-country version of the
54:2183:119963:21:20:79:533:593:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Lucas tree model with time-varying volatility and derive expressions for country-specific output
54:2184:120059:20:20:79:533:573:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:growth, equity returns and their realized volatilities in terms of innovations to a global technol-
54:2185:120158:20:21:79:533:553:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:ogy or growth factor and its higher–order moments.  We show that both a level (or first-order)
54:2186:120252:21:20:79:533:532:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:common  component  and  higher-order  common  components  are  required  to  explain  the  cross
54:2187:120348:20:20:79:533:512:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:country variations of realized volatility, but only the level common component is required for
54:2188:120442:20:21:79:533:492:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:explaining cross-country differences in output growth.  Using this theoretical insight, we estimate
54:2189:120541:21:20:79:533:471:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:a multi-country econometric model in output growth and realized volatilities for 32 countries
54:2190:120634:20:20:79:533:451:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:over the period 1993Q1-2011Q2.  Common real and financial shocks are identified assuming that
54:2191:120727:20:21:79:533:431:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:volatility and growth are driven by two common factors.  By taking a multi-country approach,
54:2192:120819:21:20:79:533:410:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:as opposed to studying a single economy in isolation, we can identify and estimate these two
54:2193:120911:20:20:79:533:390:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:factors.  Our identification strategy exploits different patterns in the correlations of volatility
54:2194:121010:20:21:79:533:370:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and output growth innovations across countries.  Evidence based on the cross-country correla-
54:2195:121103:21:20:79:533:349:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:tions of the raw data and estimated innovations accords with the assumptions made to achieve
54:2196:121195:20:23:79:144:329:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:identification.
54:2197:121210:23:20:96:533:306:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Empirically, we report three main sets of findings.  First, shocks to the real common factor
54:2198:121302:20:21:79:533:286:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:account for most of the unconditional correlation between volatility and growth in all but few
54:2199:121396:21:20:79:533:265:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:emerging market economies.  Second, the share of forecast error variance of volatility explained
54:2200:121492:20:20:79:533:245:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:by the real common factor shock and by country-specific growth shocks is less than 5 percent.
54:2201:121585:20:21:79:533:225:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Third, shocks to the financial common factor explain about 10 percent of the growth forecast
54:2202:121677:21:20:79:533:204:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:error variance, while country-specific volatility shocks explain only about 1-2 percent of country-
54:2203:121776:20:20:79:533:184:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:specific growth forecast error variance.  Moreover, when a shock to the financial common factor
54:2204:121871:20:21:79:533:164:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:is  realized,  its  negative  impact  on  country-specific  growth  is  large  and  persistent  as  typically
54:2205:121980:21:23:79:248:143:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:estimated in the existing literature.
54:2206:122017:23:20:96:533:120:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:These results imply that the endogenous component of country volatility is small and that
54:2207:122106:20:0:79:510:100:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:uncertainty is more important for the business cycle when the shocks are global in nature.
55:2208:122198:0:25:79:155:709:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:References
55:2209:122208:25:13:79:532:684:11:g_d0_f9:11:g_d0_f4:Abel, A. B.(1983):  “Optimal Investment under Uncertainty,”American  Economic  Review,

60:2370:133041:30:27:79:307:643:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:A.1    Country-specific Growth Process
60:2371:133079:27:16:79:533:616:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:One way to motivate the output growth specification, (1), is as follows. Assume a standard Cobb-
60:2372:133175:16:17:79:532:600:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Douglas production function in terms of output per worker and denote (Yit/Lit) =exp( ̃yit), real
60:2373:133271:17:16:79:533:583:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:GDP per capita,Ait=exp(ait) the country-specific level of technology,Litthe labor force, and
60:2374:133363:16:30:79:319:567:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f4:Kitthe capital stock in countryiso that we have:
60:2375:133411:30:29:172:439:537:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4: ̃yit= ln(Yit/Lit) =ait+αiln(Kit/Lit) =ait+αilog(kit)
60:2376:133464:29:30:79:529:508:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:fori= 1,2,...,N.  Further assume that the processes forLitandaitare exogenously given by
60:2377:133552:30:30:172:438:478:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f19:ln(Lit)−ln(Li,t−1) =ni,andait=ai0+  ̃git+γiat+eit
60:2378:133601:30:16:79:533:448:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:where  growth  of  labour  force,ni,  is  assumed  to  be  fixed,ai0is  an  initial  condition,   ̃giis  a
60:2379:133707:16:17:79:532:432:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:deterministic  growth  component  ofait,atis  the  log-level  of  a  stochastic  common  technology
60:2380:133806:17:16:79:532:415:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:factor, andeitis the country-specific technology shock, withγimeasuring the extent to which
60:2381:133897:16:17:79:532:399:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:countryiis exposed to the global technology factorat.  A key result from the stochastic growth
60:2382:133991:17:16:79:532:382:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:literature is that, for alli, log(kit) is ergodic and stationary, in the sense that asttends to infinity,
60:2383:134096:16:17:79:532:366:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:log(kit) tends to a time-invariant random variable, namely log(kit) = log(ki) +τit, whereτitis a
60:2384:134192:17:16:79:533:349:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:stationary process representing all country-specific forces driving the country’s business cycles
60:2385:134289:16:30:79:307:333:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(see, for instance, Lee et al., 1997).  So we have:

60:2390:134524:16:35:79:353:198:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f7:obtain equation (1), with ∆yit=yit−yi,t−1,gi=  ̃gi+ni.

70:3068:145078:40:30:79:396:232:14:g_d0_f3:14:g_d0_f3:S2    Comparison with Principal Components
70:3069:145120:30:25:79:434:202:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:S2.1    Principal Component versus Cross-sectional Averages
70:3070:145179:25:16:79:532:177:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:In what follows we compare the cross-sectional average of the GDP growth rates (∆ ̄yω,t) with the
70:3071:145276:16:16:79:555:161:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:first principal component of the individual output growth series{∆yit,i= 1,2,....,N;t= 1,2,....,T},
70:3072:145375:16:15:79:532:145:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:which we denote byPCy1,t.  As can be seen from Figure S.2, the two series (∆ ̄yω,t, andPCy1,t)
70:3073:145469:15:0:79:356:130:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:move very closely and have a correlation coefficient of 0.9.
71:3074:145531:0:16:79:533:709:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:S2.2    Principal Components of the Combined Panel of Output Growth Series
71:3075:145605:16:26:117:260:693:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:and Realized Volatilities
71:3076:145630:26:16:79:533:667:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:As  stated  in  Remark  2  and  3  in  the  main  text  of  the  paper,  applying  principal  component
71:3077:145733:16:15:79:533:651:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:analysis to the panel of all volatility series or all volatility and growth series would not permit
71:3078:145832:15:16:79:533:636:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:identifyingft.  To see this,  we extract the first two principal components from the full panel
71:3079:145927:16:15:79:533:620:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of growth rates (∆yit) and volatilities (vit),  which we label byPCvy1,tandPCvy2,t,  respectively.
71:3080:146025:15:16:79:533:605:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:We then fit a VAR(1) model to these two PCs, and compute orthogonalized residuals from this
71:3081:146116:16:17:79:532:589:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:VAR with a Cholesky decomposition placing the first PC, namelyPCvy1,t, first (as discussed in
71:3082:146209:17:0:79:383:572:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f19:Section 3.3).  We denote these orthogonalized residuals by-PC
71:3083:146270:0:7:383:391:581:6:g_d0_f15:6:g_d0_f15:vy
71:3084:146272:7:0:382:436:574:6:g_d0_f12:8:g_d0_f19:1,tand-PC
71:3085:146281:0:7:436:444:581:6:g_d0_f15:6:g_d0_f15:vy
71:3086:146283:7:17:435:532:574:6:g_d0_f12:11:g_d0_f4:2,t.  Figure S.3 plots
71:3087:146305:17:0:79:96:557:11:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f19:-PC
71:3088:146308:0:8:96:104:565:6:g_d0_f15:6:g_d0_f15:vy1,t
71:3089:146313:8:0:109:286:557:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f19:together withˆζt(top panel) and-PC
71:3090:146347:0:8:286:295:565:6:g_d0_f15:6:g_d0_f15:vy2,t
71:3091:146352:8:16:299:532:557:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:together withˆξt(bottom panel), and shows that
71:3092:146398:16:34:79:532:541:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the two series behave in a very different fashion, with correlations of−0.43 and 0.43 respectively.
71:3093:146497:34:26:79:379:507:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:S2.3    Applying Principal Components Recursively
71:3094:146546:26:15:79:533:481:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:While principal components extracted from the panel of all volatility and growth series do not
71:3095:146640:15:16:79:532:466:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:permit  identifyingft,  here  we  show  how  principal  component  analysis  can  be  used  to  obtain
71:3096:146742:16:15:79:533:450:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:estimates of the real and financial factors reported in the paper.  As discussed in the paper, we
71:3097:146839:15:16:79:533:435:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:need to follow a recursive procedure where the order of the recursion plays a crucial role.  We
71:3098:146934:16:16:79:533:419:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:need extract the first principal component from the panel of GDP growth rates, which as before
71:3099:147028:16:15:79:532:403:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:we label byPCy1,t, and as noted earlier recovers a consistent estimator ofζt(up to an scalar).
71:3100:147122:15:16:79:533:388:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Next, we obtain the first principal component from the combined panel of output growth rates
71:3101:147214:16:15:79:533:372:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and volatilities and label it asPCvy1,t.  Then, we estimate a VAR(1) in the principal components
71:3102:147310:15:16:79:533:357:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:(PCy1,t,PCvy1,t)′to remove any serial correlation, and orthogonalize the residuals of this VAR with
71:3103:147409:16:15:79:533:341:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:a Cholesky factorization of the variance-covariance matrix of this VAR’s reduced form residuals,
71:3104:147505:15:0:79:453:326:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f19:withPCy1,tordered first.  Denote the resultant orthogonalized residuals by-PC
71:3105:147582:0:8:453:461:334:6:g_d0_f15:6:g_d0_f15:y1,t
71:3106:147586:8:0:466:504:326:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f19:and-PC
71:3107:147592:0:8:505:513:334:6:g_d0_f15:6:g_d0_f15:vy1,t
71:3108:147597:8:20:514:517:326:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:.
71:3109:147598:20:0:96:196:306:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f19:Figure  S.4  plots-PC
71:3110:147619:0:8:196:205:314:6:g_d0_f15:6:g_d0_f15:y1,t
71:3111:147623:8:0:211:395:306:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f19:together  withˆζt(top  panel)  and-PC
71:3112:147660:0:8:395:403:314:6:g_d0_f15:6:g_d0_f15:vy1,t
71:3113:147665:8:16:409:532:306:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:together  withˆξt(bottom
71:3114:147689:16:16:79:532:290:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:panel), and shows that they move in tandem, with correlations of 0.82 and 0.97, respectively.
71:3115:147782:16:15:79:533:274:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Note, finally, that if we were to do a Cholesky factorization of the residuals from the same VAR
71:3116:147878:15:16:79:532:259:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:but with the variables ordered in reverse, namely (PCvy1,t,PCy1,t,)′, the resultant orthogonalized
71:3117:147976:16:15:79:532:243:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:residuals will not closely followˆζtandˆξt.  We conclude from this exercise that principal compo-
71:3118:148073:15:16:79:533:228:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:nent analysis could be used to obtain qualitatively similar results that we report in the paper if
71:3119:148171:16:0:79:303:212:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:applied in the recursive manner proposed here.

75:3309:151694:18:16:96:532:659:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f19:As a first order approximation, therefore, we will assume that the covariance matrix ofθt

75:3326:152448:16:15:79:533:420:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:allow for non-zero correlations across the idiosyncratic errors.  The two sets of impulse responses
75:3327:152547:15:34:79:319:405:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:coincide if the covariance matrix ofθtis diagonal.
75:3328:152597:34:26:79:355:371:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:S3.2    Forecast Error Variance Decompositions
75:3329:152643:26:15:79:533:345:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Traditionally,  the  forecast  error  variance  decomposition  of  a  VAR  model  is  performed  on  a
75:3330:152745:15:16:79:532:330:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:set of orthogonalized shocks, whereby the contribution of thejthorthogonalized innovation to
75:3331:152837:16:16:79:532:314:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:the mean square error of then-step ahead forecast of the model is calculated.  In our empirical
75:3332:152932:16:15:79:533:298:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:application this is not the case as —even if the country-specific volatility and growth innovations
75:3333:153031:15:16:79:533:283:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f4:ηitandεitare weakly correlated across countries— some pairs of innovations can still display
75:3334:153123:16:15:79:533:267:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:some non-zero correlation.  An alternative approach is to compute Generalized Forecast Error
75:3335:153215:15:16:79:532:252:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Variance Decompositions (GV D) of Pesaran and Shin (1998).  The Generalized Forecast Error
75:3336:153305:16:16:79:532:236:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Variance Decompositions consider the proportion of the variance of then-step forecast errors
75:3337:153397:16:15:79:533:220:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of the endogenous variables that is explained by conditioning on the non-orthogonalized shocks,
75:3338:153492:15:16:79:533:205:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:while  explicitly  allowing  for  the  contemporaneous  correlations  between  these  shocks  and  the
75:3339:153594:16:18:79:290:189:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:shocks to the other equations in the system.
75:3340:153638:18:16:96:532:171:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:LetGV Di,ζ,nandGV Di,ξ,nbe the share of then-step ahead forecast error variance of the
75:3341:153724:16:0:79:532:155:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f4:ithvariable inztthat is accounted for byζtandξt, respectively, andGV Di,jthe variance share
76:3342:153817:0:46:79:273:709:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:of a generic country-specific shock, then:
76:3343:153859:46:0:111:173:663:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f4:GV Di,ζ,n=
76:3344:153869:0:20:228:237:688:8:g_d0_f19:11:g_d0_f21:n∑
76:3345:153871:20:0:224:238:668:8:g_d0_f19:8:g_d0_f5:`=0
76:3346:153874:0:19:240:284:678:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f5:(e′iA`sf)2
76:3347:153884:19:20:189:198:659:8:g_d0_f19:11:g_d0_f21:n∑
76:3348:153886:20:0:185:199:639:8:g_d0_f19:8:g_d0_f5:`=0
76:3349:153889:0:0:201:254:649:11:g_d0_f24:11:g_d0_f4:e′iA`A′`ei+
76:3350:153900:0:20:261:270:659:8:g_d0_f19:11:g_d0_f21:n∑
76:3351:153902:20:0:257:271:639:8:g_d0_f19:8:g_d0_f5:`=0
76:3352:153905:0:0:273:311:649:11:g_d0_f24:11:g_d0_f18:e′iC`ˆΩC
76:3353:153913:0:10:312:314:656:8:g_d0_f20:8:g_d0_f20:′
76:3354:153914:10:0:312:323:646:8:g_d0_f19:8:g_d0_f19:`ei
76:3355:153917:0:60:324:532:663:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f4:,  n= 1,2,....,H,(S3.9)
76:3356:153940:60:0:112:173:603:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f4:GV Di,ξ,n=
76:3357:153950:0:20:228:237:629:8:g_d0_f19:11:g_d0_f21:n∑

76:3365:153986:0:0:273:311:590:11:g_d0_f24:11:g_d0_f18:e′iC`ˆΩC
76:3366:153994:0:10:312:314:597:8:g_d0_f20:8:g_d0_f20:′

76:3369:154022:59:0:112:173:544:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f4:GV Di,j,n=
76:3370:154032:0:0:209:222:560:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f19:ˆω−1jj

76:3375:154053:0:31:289:300:572:11:g_d0_f21:8:g_d0_f5:)2
76:3376:154055:31:21:189:198:541:8:g_d0_f19:11:g_d0_f21:n∑
76:3377:154057:21:0:185:199:520:8:g_d0_f19:8:g_d0_f5:`=0
76:3378:154060:0:0:201:254:531:11:g_d0_f24:11:g_d0_f4:e′iA`A′`ei+

76:3383:154085:10:0:312:323:528:8:g_d0_f19:8:g_d0_f19:`ei
76:3384:154088:0:49:324:533:544:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f4:,  j= 1,2,....,2N,  n= 1,2,....,H;(S3.11)
76:3385:154129:49:15:96:533:495:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:Note that the different assumptions we make on the covariance matrix of all country-specific
76:3386:154221:15:16:79:533:480:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:shocks,ˆΩ,have implications for the error variance decompositions. Specifically, when we assume
76:3387:154316:16:15:79:532:464:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:that  (i)ˆΩis  diagonal  or  (ii)ˆΩis  block-diagonal  with  Cholesky-orthogonalized  blocks,  the
76:3388:154414:15:16:79:532:449:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:relative importance of shocks to country volatility and growth for all countries (ηitandεit, for
76:3389:154510:16:16:79:532:433:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f4:j=  1,2,....,2N)  and  shocks  to  the  two  common  factorsζtandξt,  is  easily  characterized  as
76:3390:154609:16:0:79:174:417:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f4:V Di,ζ,n+V Di,ξ,n+
76:3391:154627:0:12:177:200:426:11:g_d0_f21:8:g_d0_f19:∑2N
76:3392:154630:12:12:189:532:414:8:g_d0_f19:11:g_d0_f4:j=1V Di,j,n= 1.  That is the GVD formula coincides with the standard
76:3393:154698:12:16:79:533:402:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:VD formula.  In contrast, when we consider an unrestricted covariance matrixˆΩ, the sum of the
76:3394:154792:16:34:79:312:386:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:variance shares does not necessarily add up to 1.
76:3395:154841:34:16:79:533:352:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:S3.3    Average  Impulse  Responses  and  Forecast  Error  Variance  Decomposi-
76:3396:154920:16:25:117:145:336:12:g_d0_f3:12:g_d0_f3:tions
76:3397:154925:25:16:79:533:311:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:As a summary measure of the effects of shocks to the common factors we report the following
76:3398:155016:16:16:79:533:295:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:average measures.  Denote the impulse response (or forecast error variance decomposition) of a
76:3399:155110:16:15:79:532:279:11:g_d0_f4:8:g_d0_f20:particular shock on thejthvariable in countryiat horizonnbyXi,j,n.  Letw= (w1,w2,...,wN)′
76:3400:155199:15:16:79:532:264:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:be  a  vector  of  fixed  weights  such  that  ΣNi=1wi=  1.   Then  the  average  impulse  response  (or
76:3401:155303:16:36:79:532:248:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:forecast error variance decomposition) of the shock to variablej, at horizonn, is computed as:
76:3402:155397:36:0:255:295:212:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f4:Xω,j,n=

76:3405:155409:0:36:316:532:212:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f4:wiXi,j,n.(S3.12)
76:3406:155425:36:38:79:243:176:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:and its dispersion is computed by:
76:3407:155459:38:0:211:253:138:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f4:σXω,j,n=
76:3408:155467:0:8:257:274:156:11:g_d0_f21:8:g_d0_f19:[N
76:3409:155469:8:23:263:279:148:11:g_d0_f21:11:g_d0_f21:∑
76:3410:155470:23:0:264:278:125:8:g_d0_f19:8:g_d0_f5:i=1
76:3411:155473:0:0:281:375:138:11:g_d0_f7:8:g_d0_f5:w2i(Xi,j,n−Xω,j,n)2
76:3412:155492:0:18:376:395:156:11:g_d0_f21:8:g_d0_f5:]1/2
76:3413:155496:18:36:397:532:138:11:g_d0_f7:11:g_d0_f4:,(S3.13)
76:3414:155504:36:15:79:533:102:11:g_d0_f4:11:g_d0_f4:assuming country-specific impulse responses or forecast error variance decompositions are ap-
